###258###
That time of year thou mayst in me behold
When yellow leaves, or none, or few, do hang
Upon those boughs which shake against the cold,
Bare ruin'd choirs, where late the sweet birds sang.
In me thou see'st the twilight of such day
As after sunset fadeth in the west;
Which by and by black night doth take away,
Death's second self, that seals up all in rest.
In me thou see'st the glowing of such fire
That on the ashes of his youth doth lie,
As the death-bed whereon it must expire
Consumed with that which it was nourish'd by.
This thou perceivest, which makes thy love more strong,
To love that well which thou must leave ere long.

###259###
Were't ought to me I bore the canopy,
With my extern the outward honouring,
Or laid great bases for eternity,
Which proves more short than waste or ruining?
Have I not seen dwellers on form and favour
Lose all, and more, by paying too much rent,
For compound sweet foregoing simple savour,
Pitiful thrivers, in their folly spent?
No, let me be obsequious in thy heart,
And take all honours on their novel wing;
For thou art all my art, and dost impart
To me most rich and sumptuous adorning.
How can I then be elder than thou art?
Or make old woes new, when thou'rt youth's true heart?

###260###
When my love swears that she is made of truth,
I do believe her, though I know she lies,
That she might think me some untutor'd youth,
Unlearned in the world's false subtleties.
Thus vainly thinking that she thinks me young,
Although she knows my days are past the best,
Simply I credit her false-speaking tongue:
On both sides thus is simple truth suppress'd.
But wherefore says she not she is unjust?
And wherefore say not I that I am old?
O, love's best habit is in seeming trust,
And age in love loves not to have years told:
Therefore I lie with her and she with me,
And in our faults by lies we flatter'd be.

###261###
When lovely youth doth fade and lose its hue,
And time's swift shadows steal away thy light,
Where shall we seek for beauty, fresh and new?
Or guard thee from oblivion's endless night?

The summer's bloom doth swiftly pass away,
And winter's frost doth claim the gentle flower,
So too must every mortal thing decay,
And yield its substance to the hungry hour.

Yet in these lines thy grace shall ever dwell,
A painted image for all eyes to see,
More lasting than a life, a magic spell,
From death's cold grip to set thy spirit free.

So long as men can breathe, or eyes can scan,
My verse shall praise thee, 'gainst time's cruel plan.

###262###
Though fickle winds may shift from hour to hour,
And roses change their crimson for a pale,
Thy steadfast mind doth hold a constant power,
That doth not bend though bitter storms assail.

The summer's lease is but a season's span,
And beauty's flower is transient to behold,
So soon it fades, by nature's cruelest plan,
Leaving but winter's shadow, stark and cold.

But thy dear love, a lamp that ever gleams,
Doth light my way through sorrow and through dread,
No fading vision, born of fleeting dreams,
But firm and true, though all the world be dead.

Thus, though all else may fail and fall apart,
Thy truth remains enshrined within my heart.

###263###
When thou art absent, all the world seems grey,
And joy itself doth vanish from my sight,
Each hour doth stretch into a weary day,
And shadows deepen to an endless night.

No birdsong sweet can charm my listening ear,
Nor sunlit morn dispel my spirit's gloom,
For where thou art not, sorrow dwelleth near,
And loneliness doth fill my silent room.

I seek thy image in each passing face,
And crave the solace of thy gentle hand,
But finding none, I wander through this space,
A stranger lost within a foreign land.

Ah, come again, and banish all my pain,
Lest absence prove my life's undoing gain.

###264###
Why dost thou hoard thy beauty's tender bloom,
And keep it prisoner, meant for all to see?
To what dark end dost thou reserve thy room,
When fading hence, thy grace must swiftly flee?

Like a fair lamp that burns its oil within,
And gives no light to cheer the darkened way,
So thou dost hide the grace thou mightst have been,
And let thy youthful prime thus waste away.

The fleeting hours, like thieves, do steal apace,
And from thy cheek shall pluck the rosy hue,
Then wrinkled age shall mar thy lovely face,
And what was beauty, time shall then undo.

Beget then beauty, ere thou reach thy tomb,
Lest all thy fairness vanish in the gloom.

###265###
When Time, the fell destroyer, with his hand,
Shall sweep away all that we deem so fair,
And beauty's structure, built on shifting sand,
Doth vanish quite, dissolving into air;

What then remains of earth's most glorious show?
The proudest towers brought low by slow decay,
And all that blossomed, now lies cold below,
Consumed by shadows of a former day.

No earthly power can stay his swift decree,
Nor gilded monuments his wrath defy,
For he doth claim all things, both wild and free,
And watches kingdoms rise, and then to die.

Yet steadfast love, though all around may cease,
Shall find in faith its never-ending peace.

###266###
Those eyes, which hold the heaven's purest light,
And with their beams my darkest soul do grace,
Are stars that guide me through the deepest night,
And banish shadows from this earthly space.

No earthly gem with such a brilliance gleams,
Nor morning dew can hold so fair a hue,
They are the fount of my most cherished dreams,
And in their depths I find my spirit true.

A silent language in their glances plays,
Where truth and virtue exquisitely entwine,
To lead my spirit through life's intricate ways,
And make my mortal essence feel divine.

Oh, blessed sight, that doth my soul enthral,
Thou art my sun, my universe, my all.

###267###
The fragile flower doth blossom in the morn,
And by the eve its tender petals fall,
So brief a life, so soon to be forlorn,
Obedient to nature's urgent call.

We gaze upon the sun's declining ray,
And know that darkness soon will fill the air,
Each vibrant moment slips too swift away,
Leaving behind but sorrow and despair.

What then are we, whose days are but a breath?
A transient spark 'twixt darkness and the light,
Each fleeting step doth lead us on to death,
And plunge our being into endless night.

Yet in the heart, love's flame may brightly burn,
And from its ashes, hope shall yet return.

###268###
When sweetest music with its silver sound,
Doth steal into the chambers of mine ear,
And harmony through every note is found,
Dispelling all the shadows of my fear;

I muse on how this concord sweet doth bind
Each separate string to make a perfect whole,
A gentle echo of a loving mind,
That doth control and soothe my restless soul.

Ah, would that love itself might ever prove
So well attuned, without a jarring tone,
A tender union, like the notes above,
Where every spirit to its own is known.

But oft, alas, doth discord's harshness start,
And mar the music of a single heart.

###269###
Those eyes, that hold a heaven within their blue,
And with a glance can soothe the troubled breast,
Reflect a soul eternally so true,
And bid my weary spirit find its rest.

No painter's brush, how cunning e'er it be,
Can capture half the magic that they keep,
For in their depths a universe I see,
Where silent thoughts in mystic slumber sleep.

They speak a language that no tongue can frame,
A gentle force that conquers every fear,
And at their light, my troubled heart takes flame,
Dispelling all the shadows dwelling near.

So let them gaze, and let my spirit yield,
To truth and beauty, openly revealed.

###270###
Make thou no more excuse, but bravely strive
To give thy beauty to a future age,
Lest, unbegotten, it should cease to thrive,
And perish with thee on life's fleeting stage.

For nature's debt must ever be repaid,
And loveliness must pass to loveliness,
Else is its precious essence quite unmade,
And beauty dies, for want of due address.

Look in thy glass, and tell me what thou see'st,
A perfect form, that soon must fade to dust,
Oh, yield thy self, ere age doth make thee least,
And leave no image that we may entrust.

Then live anew, when thou art past thy prime,
And mock the ravage of destructive time.

###271###
The gentle spring, with garlands fresh and green,
Doth bid the frost and barren winter cease,
And paints the meadows with a joyful sheen,
Awakening all the world to newfound peace.

But quickly comes the summer, warm and bright,
To crown the year with harvest's golden store,
Then autumn follows, stealing day from night,
And strips the trees of what they held before.

So human life, from childhood's tender dawn,
Through vigorous youth, and age's slow decline,
Doth pass as swiftly as a summer's morn,
And leaves behind but mem'ries, faint and fine.

Yet in the heart, where truth and love reside,
A brighter season ever shall abide.

###272###
When fickle Fortune turns her back on me,
And with a frown doth steal my cheer away,
I ponder on the fate that binds me free,
And clouds my sunshine with a dismal day.

My hopes, like ships, are tossed upon the foam,
And every venture meets a bitter end,
No calm respite, no solace to call home,
Nor trusted comfort from a loyal friend.

Why doth she mock with gifts she soon reclaims?
And lift me high, to cast me down again?
My spirit aches, consumed by hidden flames,
And sighs for ease that it may not attain.

Yet in my love, I find a constant grace,
Which time nor sorrow ever can efface.

###273###
Let no man say that love is but a breath,
A fleeting shadow, born of fancy's play,
To change its course, or yield itself to death,
When tribulations mark the weary way.

No, true love stands, a beacon ever bright,
Unmoved by tempests, constant as the pole,
It is the star that guides through darkest night,
The sovereign balm that doth make spirits whole.

It suffers patiently, and seeks no praise,
But gives itself without a thought of gain,
And lights the path through life's perplexing maze,
Defying winter, sunshine, wind, and rain.

If this be error, and upon me proved,
I never writ, nor no man ever loved.

###274###
Thou art too fair to let thy beauty waste,
A rosebud opening to the morning dew,
Designed by nature, in such lovely haste,
To bless the world with charms forever new.

But if thou dost withhold thy vital spark,
And let thy springtime perish with thy breath,
Then all thy promise fades into the dark,
And gives thy fairness to the maw of death.

For what is beauty, if it bear no fruit?
A treasure buried, never brought to light,
A silent song, plucked from a broken lute,
That fades unheard into the endless night.

Oh, be not cruel, but let thy love increase,
And give to life thy beauty's sweet release.

###275###
The transient joy that brightens up my day,
Like morning mist, doth vanish with the sun,
And leaves my spirit desolate to stray,
Ere half its brief, sweet journey is begun.

I seize the moment, holding it so fast,
Lest it escape upon the winged breeze,
But even as I grasp, it is past,
And I am left with sorrow and unease.

The laughter loud, the jest, the merry tune,
How quickly do they fade into the air,
Beneath the gaze of an indifferent moon,
And leave behind but echoes of despair.

So learn, my soul, that bliss is but a guest,
And in its absence, patience is the test.

###276###
Behold the ocean, restless and profound,
Whose mighty waves defy the human will,
No fragile bark upon its bosom bound,
Can long withstand its power, surging still.

The mountains stand, colossal, proud, and grand,
Unchanged through ages, heedless of man's plight,
While kingdoms rise and fall throughout the land,
They pierce the heavens with eternal light.

The storm-tossed cloud, that doth the tempest bring,
Unleashes fury on the trembling earth,
No mortal art can clip its mighty wing,
Nor alter nature's elemental birth.

So small are we, beneath creation's span,
A fleeting shadow in God's cosmic plan.

###277###
When heavy thoughts do press upon my soul,
And sorrow's clouds obscure life's joyous view,
My weary spirit yields to their control,
And finds no comfort, save in thoughts of you.

For in thy friendship, I a haven find,
A shelter safe from every bitter storm,
A gentle solace for my troubled mind,
That keeps my doubting heart forever warm.

No flattering tongue, nor false and hollow praise,
Can stir such loyalty as thine doth show,
Thou light'st my path through life's perplexing maze,
And help'st my burdened spirit onward go.

So blessèd be the hour when first we met,
A faithful friend, I never shall forget.

###278###
When fleeting beauty fades to dust away,
And youth's bright spark doth vanish from the gaze,
What hand can stay the ruin of decay,
Or rescue grace from time's consuming maze?

The sculptor's art may carve a noble form,
And painter's skill immortal hues bestow,
But these are frail, defenseless 'gainst the storm,
And yield to winter's unforgiving snow.

Yet in these humble lines, thy spirit bright
Shall find a mirror, radiant and clear,
A beacon shining through eternal night,
Dispelling every doubt and every fear.

For in this verse, thy truth shall ever last,
Long after earthly glories are past.

###279###
How can I swear my love shall always hold,
When nature's law decrees that all must fade?
The freshest flower turns to withered mold,
And beauty's promise is too soon betrayed.

No oath can bind the fickle turning tide,
Nor fervent vow arrest the winged hour,
For time doth laugh at pledges, side by side,
And plucks the petals from the strongest flower.

Yet in this doubt, my faith doth still endure,
That what is true, no moment can erase,
A constant flame, eternally so pure,
That finds its solace in thy gentle grace.

Though all things change, and swiftly pass away,
My love for thee shall know no changing day.

###280###
As perfect form as ever nature made,
Endowed with beauty, truth, and gentle mien,
No flaw within thy lovely mold is laid,
Thou art the fairest that was ever seen.

The morning sun doth borrow from thine eye
A brighter lustre for his golden ray,
And stars at night, when thou art passing by,
Do pale their fires, ashamed to light the way.

No artifice doth paint thy rosy cheek,
Nor borrowed tints thy peerless grace impart,
But all thy charms, a silent language speak,
And captivate each longing, loving heart.

So wholly good, so utterly divine,
All excellence in thee doth brightly shine.

###281###
When fresh-born blossoms ope to morning's light,
And tender youth its golden prime displays,
So swiftly passeth beauty from our sight,
Ere wrinkles trace their sorrow-furrowed ways.
The fleeting hour doth steal each summer grace,
And envious age doth spoil what once was fair;
No earthly power may hold it in its place,
But all must yield to time's relentless snare.
Yet shall my verse, though rude and simply wrought,
Preserve thy memory from oblivion's dust,
So long as men shall read or hold thee sought,
Against time's cruel and all-devouring rust.
So live thou ever, in this lasting rhyme,
And mock the scythe of all-consuming Time.

###282###
My love for thee doth mock the changing moon,
Which wanes and grows, uncertain in its phase;
It hath no ebb, nor knoweth any noon,
But shines with steady, unextinguished blaze.
Let fickle fortune frown or softly smile,
Let seasons shift and swift years hurry by,
Thy constant heart shall my true soul beguile,
And hold its sovereign sway until I die.
For though the rose its crimson leaves let fall,
And winter winds do strip the forest bare,
My faith in thee shall stand beyond them all,
A steadfast rock against all worldly care.
Thus, whilst I live, no falsehood shall I prove,
But loyal be unto my dearest love.

###283###
Shall I compare thy grace to summer's day?
Thou art more mild and hold'st a fairer light.
Rough winds do shake the darling buds of May,
And summer's lease hath all too short a night.
Sometime too hot the eye of heaven doth burn,
And often is his gold complexion dimmed;
And every fair from fair sometime must turn,
By chance or nature's changing course untrimmed.
But thy eternal summer shall not fade,
Nor lose possession of that worth thou ow'st,
Nor shall death brag thou wander'st in his shade,
When in eternal lines to time thou grow'st.
So long as men can breathe, or eyes can see,
So long lives this, and this gives life to thee.

###284###
The breath of dawn, which doth the darkness chase,
Doth oft precede a day of cloudy gloom;
So joy doth vanish, leaving sorrow's trace,
And hopeful flowers give way to dusty tomb.
What trust may frail humanity repose
In earthly gifts, which swift as shadows fly?
A transient bliss, which no man truly knows,
Ere it doth fade beneath a weeping sky.
Yet in thy truth, a steadfast star I find,
A guiding light when all the world seems lost,
A balm to soothe the troubled, weary mind,
Worth more than empire, or a kingdom's cost.
For in thy heart, no fleeting change I see,
But constancy, which bindeth me to thee.

###285###
When nature's cunning hand with lavish store
Hath wrought the forms of beauty to behold,
She doth but lend, and asks for payment more,
And all her treasures turn to dust and mould.
The fairest flower, that lifts its gentle head,
Must soon resign its glory to the ground;
And all the vibrant life, so richly fed,
By winter's icy breath is quickly drowned.
But thou, whose essence shines beyond decay,
Whose spirit knows no fading or decline,
Dost banish shadows with thy glorious ray,
A lasting monument, a soul divine.
So, though the world its fleeting shows doth boast,
My constant heart to thee is given most.

###286###
How oft I sigh, when absence holds thee far,
And cruel distance doth our souls divide!
Each sun-lit day seems like a dreary star,
And shadows lengthen where thy joys abide.
My weary thoughts, like pilgrims, take their flight,
To seek thy presence in some distant land;
They find thee not, and sink in darkest night,
And leave my spirit chained by sorrow's hand.
Then do I chide the sun for shining bright,
And curse the moon that lights a lonely way,
Wishing for swift return of morning's light,
To bring thee back, and banish my dismay.
Come back, my love, and banish every fear,
For joy returns when thy sweet form is near.

###287###
The aged year, when winter doth approach,
Lays bare the boughs where summer's green did thrive;
So doth my spirit feel time's cold encroachment,
And sees its youthful passions cease to live.
No more the fire that once did brightly burn,
No more the songs that thrilled the morning air;
But silent thoughts to graver matters turn,
And contemplation banishes all care.
Yet, as the earth doth hold within its breast
The promise of a spring to come again,
So in my heart thy image finds its rest,
And gives me solace through life's bitter rain.
Though flesh doth fade and earthly joys grow old,
Thy love's a treasure, brighter than fine gold.

###288###
When envious tongues thy spotless name assail,
And malice seeks thy reputation's stain,
My loyal heart shall never turn nor quail,
But rise to prove thy virtue once again.
They know thee not, who judge by outward show,
Nor pierce the depths where truth and honour lie;
Their shallow minds no deeper currents know,
But by false rumour let their judgments fly.
But I, who know the essence of thy soul,
Whose every thought doth mirror truth's pure light,
Will stand for thee, though storms around us roll,
And champion thy cause with all my might.
For slander's breath, howe'er it strives to sting,
Cannot corrupt the truth that thou dost bring.

###289###
My mind, like to a restless, feathered bird,
Doth seek its solace in thy gentle gaze;
At every absence, its deep cry is heard,
And pines for comforts of thy sunlit days.
No painted scene, nor beauty wrought by art,
Can hold its gaze as can thy living grace;
No dulcet tone can soothe my troubled heart,
Like but a whisper from thy lovely face.
For in thy form, all heaven's glories dwell,
A mirror where my truest joys I see;
A magic charm, a sweet and potent spell,
That binds my yearning spirit fast to thee.
So let me dwell where thy dear presence lies,
And lose myself within thy loving eyes.

###290###
The merchant, fearing rocks and ocean's rage,
Secures his goods against the watery tomb;
The miser hoards his gold from every age,
Lest poverty should seal his bitter doom.
But I, whose treasure doth in thee reside,
Can find no fortress strong enough to keep
Thy precious worth safe from the world's harsh tide,
Nor wakeful guard against oblivion's sleep.
Save this alone: that in these lines of mine,
Thy peerless beauty shall forever bloom;
A living spirit, deathless and divine,
Escaping time's inexorable gloom.
So let the world its transient riches crave,
My greater wealth in thee, this verse shall save.

###291###
What alchemy doth hold such wondrous sway,
That turns to gold the moments spent with thee?
The leaden hours then brightly gleam and play,
And life's dull dross becomes pure ecstasy.
When thou art near, the world doth lose its grey,
The very air doth breathe a sweeter scent;
And sorrows that did vex me through the day,
Are by thy gentle presence softly rent.
No magic spell, nor charm of ancient lore,
Could work such transformation on my soul;
For in thy love, I find a boundless store
Of joy that makes my broken spirit whole.
Thus, though all other wonders fade and flee,
My greatest marvel is to live with thee.

###292###
When I behold the proudest works of man,
The crumbling tower, the palace turned to dust,
I see how frail is every earthly plan,
And how all glory yields to time's slow rust.
The mightiest oak, that braves a hundred years,
Must finally bow beneath the tempest's hand;
The crystal stream, that through the valley steers,
Is lost within the vastness of the sand.
And then I think upon thy fleeting grace,
Thy youthful beauty, destined to decay;
And how death's shadow soon will hide thy face,
And sweep thy loveliness from earth away.
Unless these lines a monument can be,
To grant eternal life, my love, to thee.

###293###
My heart, once swift and eager for delight,
Now beats a measured rhythm, calm and low;
Its youthful fires, quenched by time's cold night,
No longer with such ardent passion glow.
The dreams that once like soaring eagles flew,
Now perch upon the bough of sober thought;
And all the false allurements I once knew,
By wiser judgment are to nothing brought.
Yet in this change, a deeper truth I find,
A clearer vision of what truly lasts;
And unto thee, my constant, faithful mind,
Its anchor holds against life's bitter blasts.
For love like ours, refined by passing years,
Outlives the tide of earthly hopes and fears.

###294###
Let others praise the dawn's resplendent hue,
Or marvel at the stars in heavens high;
Let poets laud the ocean's boundless blue,
Or sing of flowers that bloom and swiftly die.
My simple muse doth seek a fairer theme,
No transient gleam, no beauty soon to cease;
But that dear spirit, like a waking dream,
Which fills my weary soul with quiet peace.
Thy steadfast virtues are the stars I trace,
Thy gentle kindness is the dawn I see;
The purest ocean in thy loving grace,
And endless spring in thy felicity.
So let them wander, seeking what they may,
My only joy is found in thee each day.

###295###
The bitter pangs that absence doth impart,
Do teach my soul the measure of thy worth;
Each lonely hour reveals within my heart,
The hollow void, where joy had given birth.
As parched earth longs for heaven's gentle rain,
And weary trav'lers seek the morning's ray,
So doth my spirit languish in its pain,
Until thy radiant presence lights my way.
No trivial thought can fill the space thou leav'st,
No fleeting pleasure ease my deep regret;
For every comfort my sad soul bereaves,
Unless thy dear remembrance I have met.
So haste, my love, and banish my despair,
For life without thee is a thorny care.

###296###
When first I saw thy face, a wondrous sight,
My soul was captive, bound by beauty's chain;
A sudden rapture, stealing through the night,
Awakened feelings I had sought to restrain.
Like mariners, who long the shore have sought,
And find at last a haven calm and deep,
So by thy charm my wandering heart was caught,
And found the promise that its dreams would keep.
No eloquent phrase can truly then express
The silent language that my spirit knew;
A joyful yielding, a sweet willingness
To bind my future fast, my love, to you.
And from that moment, steadfast I remain,
Till life doth cease, and death dissolves my pain.

###297###
The gaudy pomp that earthly power doth wield,
And brittle fame that fades with swift decline,
Cannot compare to truth by thee revealed,
A lasting glory, purer and divine.
Let kings command, and empires rise and fall,
Let common tongues speak praises to the great;
Their fleeting triumphs answer nature's call,
And bow to destiny's unyielding state.
But thy integrity, a constant flame,
Burns ever bright, untouched by worldly strife;
And virtue's crown doth consecrate thy name,
A monument to everlasting life.
So let me cling to what is truly strong,
And in thy truth, my spirit shall belong.

###298###
My thoughts, like clouds that drift across the sky,
Are ever changing, with each passing breeze;
They seek new wonders, wheresoe'er they fly,
And find small comfort in life's transient ease.
But when they turn, dear love, to think on thee,
A sudden stillness settles on my breast;
And all the restless spirit finds decree,
In thy calm haven, where it finds its rest.
No anxious doubt then clouds my inner sight,
No vain desire can tempt my heart astray;
For in thy goodness, shining ever bright,
I find a solace for each passing day.
So let my mind on thee forever dwell,
And break the binding of each earthly spell.

###299###
When gentle sleep hath sealed my weary eyes,
And dreams, like shadows, flit across my mind,
Thy image then, in softened guise, doth rise,
And leaves all waking sorrows far behind.
I walk with thee through groves of endless green,
Where silver streams in murmuring music flow;
And in thy smile, a joy I've rarely seen,
Doth set my slumbering spirit all aglow.
But when the cock's shrill crow doth break my rest,
And morning's light dispels the dream's sweet haze,
A sudden sorrow fills my aching breast,
To find thee gone, in life's accustomed ways.
Ah, would that sleep could hold thee ever near,
And banish waking's cold and bitter tear!

###300###
O, what a grief, to see the world grow cold,
And summer's vibrant beauty turn to grey!
The tales of youth by wrinkled age are told,
As swiftly all things hasten to decay.
The golden locks, that once did softly gleam,
Are touched with silver, by time's chilling hand;
And bright eyes dim, as from a waking dream,
As memory fades, like prints upon the sand.
Yet in these lines, a solace I have found,
A sacred space where beauty may reside;
Where thy fair image, ever freshly crowned,
Shall still endure, though centuries have died.
So live thou here, in everlasting prime,
Defying death, and conquering all time.

###301###
When cruel Time, with wrinkles, mars the brow,
And steals away the beauty of thy youth,
Then shall I ask if still thou lov'st me now,
And find within thy faithful heart the truth.
For transient joys, like blossoms, quickly die,
And earthly grace doth fade as swiftly fast,
But love, which dwells within the constant eye,
A firmer bond than fleeting days can cast.
So let the seasons bring their chilling change,
And wintry blasts upon the branches blow,
My steadfast heart shall know no wider range,
But ever in thy constant favour grow.
    Thus, whilst I live, thy worth shall I proclaim,
    And deathless verse shall guard thy precious name.

###302###
Shall I compare thy grace to summer's day?
Thou art more fair, and temperately art kind:
Rough winds do shake the darling buds of May,
And summer's lease hath all too short a mind.
Sometime too hot the eye of heaven doth shine,
And oft is his gold complexion quite obscured;
And every fair from fair sometime decline,
By chance, or nature's changing course, uncur'd.
But thy eternal summer shall not fade,
Nor lose possession of that fair thou ow'st,
Nor shall Death brag thou wander'st in his shade,
When in eternal lines to time thou grow'st.
    So long as men can breathe, or eyes can see,
    So long lives this, and this gives life to thee.

###303###
The mind, distraught with cares of earthly things,
Doth oft forget the solace of true love;
And fleeting joys, on borrowed, airy wings,
Do bear us far from blessings from above.
But when thy gentle visage doth appear,
A sudden calm doth on my spirit fall,
Dispelling doubt and vanquishing all fear,
And making sense of life's discordant call.
For in thine eyes, a steadfast light I find,
That guides my steps through shadows of the night,
A beacon true, a haven for my mind,
And fills my soul with ever-fresh delight.
    Let worldly storms rage on with fierce disdain,
    My love for thee shall constantly remain.

###304###
When I behold the heavens' starry sphere,
And mark the wanderings of the moon so pale,
I then recall thy beauty, held so dear,
Whose gentle light doth over all prevail.
For greater lustre in thy face doth dwell,
Than all the gems that crown the brow of night,
And with a charm, no mortal tongue can tell,
Thou dost illuminate my spirit's sight.
No greater joy mine eye hath e'er surveyed,
No sweeter solace found my troubled breast,
Than by thy grace, my weary soul is swayed,
And in thy presence finds its perfect rest.
    Thus, heaven's wonders though they brightly gleam,
    Are but a shadow of thy beauteous dream.

###305###
My heavy heart, with sorrow overcast,
Doth pine for thee, whose absence I lament;
Each fleeting hour seems like an age to last,
With painful thoughts, my lonely days are spent.
The sun doth rise, but brings no warmth to me,
The birds do sing, but joy they cannot bring;
For all the world seems barren, wanting thee,
And mute my soul, that once did gladly sing.
Oh, haste thee back, and banish my despair,
Restore the colours to my faded view,
Let thy dear smile drive sorrow from the air,
And make my weary spirit strong and new.
    Come, sweet return, and end this bitter strife,
    And breathe again the essence of my life.

###306###
The gentle spring, with blossoms freshly born,
Doth deck the fields in robes of verdant hue;
And nature wakes to greet the early morn,
With fragrant breath, and skies of clearest blue.
Yet all this beauty, though it charms the eye,
Holds not the power thy gentle grace doth hold;
For in thy face, more heavenly tints do lie,
Than all the treasures earth can e'er unfold.
The rose may blush, the lily show its white,
The violet may its sweet perfume impart,
But none can match thy pure, celestial light,
That shines with truth within thy tender heart.
    So, when I gaze on thee, all else grows dim,
    And praise for thee becomes my only hymn.

###307###
Should time's stern hand erase all that is fair,
And crumbling stones attest to ancient might,
Then what remains of beauty, rich and rare,
When darkness claims the last remaining light?
Not brass, nor stone, nor earth, nor boundless sea,
But gentle verse, where living truth is spun,
Can hold the memory of thy grace for me,
And shield thy worth from what time hath undone.
For whilst the world shall rage in fierce assay,
And kingdoms fall to dust, and empires cease,
My humble lines shall live beyond decay,
And give thy beauty an eternal peace.
    So shall thy youth, in these poor rhymes, reside,
    When all the monuments of pride have died.

###308###
My love for thee, a fervent, constant fire,
Doth burn within my soul with endless gleam;
It doth transcend all earthly, base desire,
And makes my waking life a blessed dream.
For in thy virtues, I behold a light,
That shames the sun, and puts the stars to flight;
Thou art my guide through shadows of the night,
My refuge true, my solace and delight.
No hardship e'er can make my spirit quail,
No bitter tempest shake my firm resolve,
My steadfast heart shall never, never fail,
As circling seasons endlessly revolve.
    So long as breath doth animate my frame,
    So long shall I adore thy sacred name.

###309###
If all the world were plunged in darkest night,
And every star withdrew its friendly ray,
Thy gentle smile would bring a wondrous light,
And chase the shadows from my weary way.
For in its curve, such tender grace doth lie,
A silent promise whispered to my soul,
That banishes each tear from sorrow's eye,
And makes my wounded spirit strong and whole.
No painted art can capture such a charm,
No poet's words can truly do it right;
It shields my heart from every mortal harm,
And fills my lonely hours with pure delight.
    Thus, when thou smil'st, a heavenly bliss I prove,
    And know the boundless measure of thy love.

###310###
The proudest towers, that pierce the azure sky,
Do yield at last to time's relentless sway;
And mortal grandeur, made to catch the eye,
Like summer flowers, doth quickly fade away.
But love, unmov'd by fortune's fickle spin,
Doth scorn the triumphs that ambition craves;
Its realm is found, eternally, within,
Beyond the reach of all life's stormy waves.
Let earthly kings contend for fleeting power,
And chase the shadows of an empty fame;
I ask no more than in thy loving bower,
To cherish still thy sweet and gentle name.
    For in thy heart, my truest riches lie,
    A treasure brighter than the stars on high.

###311###
When I consider life's uncertain stage,
And how each moment swiftly takes its flight,
From youth's bright morn to sorrow's weary age,
And all is swallowed in eternal night;
I mark the rose, how fair it blooms today,
Yet ere the sun hath run its daily course,
Its vibrant petals swiftly fall away,
Succumbing to decay's relentless force.
So, too, doth beauty fade, and strength decline,
And all that's cherished yields to dusty doom;
No mortal power can stay this swift design,
But all must journey to the silent tomb.
    Yet in my heart, thy image shall remain,
    Proof 'gainst the ravage of time's bitter pain.

###312###
My spirit, oft in melancholy bound,
Doth wander lost through labyrinths of doubt;
No sweet repose my troubled soul hath found,
Until thy radiant presence puts them out.
Like barren lands, that thirst for gentle rain,
My parched desires long only for thy sight;
To ease the burden of my secret pain,
And fill my darkened world with glorious light.
For in thy glance, a healing balm I feel,
A magic touch that makes my spirit whole;
Thy tender words, like music, sweetly steal,
And bring a solace to my weary soul.
    Thus, by thy grace, transformed I stand anew,
    And find my truest self, reflected true.

###313###
The golden sun, that warms the fertile earth,
Doth call forth blossoms of a fleeting hue;
They come to life, enjoy their brief, bright birth,
Then bid the world a sorrowful adieu.
So too, doth beauty, born of flesh and blood,
A transient glory, destined to decay;
No art can stay the swiftly flowing flood,
That bears all mortal loveliness away.
But hadst thou borne a child, a living grace,
Thy fairer form would not be lost to blight;
A second self, to fill thy vacant place,
And keep thy memory shining ever bright.
    Then, though thou fade, thy beauty would survive,
    And in thy offspring, brightly would it live.

###314###
No earthly jewel, however rich and rare,
Can match the lustre of thy gentle mind;
No painted canvas, beautiful and fair,
Reflects the virtues that in thee I find.
For wisdom dwells within thy thoughtful breast,
And kindness guides thy words, and all thy ways;
Thy generous spirit puts my heart at rest,
And fills my lonely, solitary days.
The world may praise the fleeting shows of might,
And shallow fame may crown the proud and bold,
But thine's a grace, whose pure and constant light,
Is worth more than a mine of purest gold.
    Thus, in thy truth, a perfect joy I see,
    And owe my best of praises unto thee.

###315###
When Death, that hungry tyrant, comes to claim
The fairest forms, and lays all beauty low,
And seeks to blot from memory thy name,
And steal the grace that makes thy spirit glow;
Then shall my love, a shield against his power,
Defy his scythe, and mock his empty boast;
And in these lines, beyond his darkest hour,
Thy deathless virtues shall be treasured most.
For love, more strong than any mortal might,
Can build a fortress 'gainst the gaping tomb;
And cast upon thy worth a lasting light,
To triumph over sorrow and all gloom.
    So shalt thou live, when marble turns to dust,
    Preserv'd in lines of truth and endless trust.

###316###
My humble pen, though striving for thy praise,
Doth oft fall short of thy deserving worth;
And all my words, in these poor, feeble lays,
Are but a shadow of thy gentle birth.
For how can language, finite and so weak,
Encompass all the graces of thy soul?
When every thought, aspiring, fain would speak
Of that perfection which doth make thee whole.
The sun itself, with all its golden ray,
Cannot illuminate thy spirit's light;
Nor can the morn, with breaking of the day,
Dispel the shadows of my humble plight.
    So pardon, then, this poor and weak address,
    Which strives for praise, yet achieves nothing less.

###317###
When trials come, and burdens press me sore,
And worldly cares besiege my weary mind,
I turn to thee, and ask for nothing more,
Than in thy gentle presence peace to find.
For in this world, where strife and envy dwell,
And falsehood often wears a pleasing face,
Thy steadfast heart doth cast a potent spell,
And fills my anxious spirit with sweet grace.
Let others chase the fleeting breath of fame,
And seek for riches in a barren field;
I find my joy in speaking of thy name,
And know to whom my loyalties must yield.
    So, come what may, through sunshine or through storm,
    Thy constant love shall keep my spirit warm.

###318###
The bitter memories of sorrows past,
Like phantom ships, do haunt my troubled sleep;
And former joys, too beautiful to last,
Do make my eyes in silent anguish weep.
But when I call to mind thy faithful heart,
And all the kindness thou hast shown to me,
Then every grief and sorrow doth depart,
And leaves my weary spirit calm and free.
For in thy friendship, I have found a haven,
A quiet refuge from the world's harsh strife;
A sacred bond, by purest truth engraven,
That gives a deeper meaning to my life.
    So, come what will, though fortune's frown descend,
    My loyal heart shall love thee to the end.

###319###
When first I saw thy face, a wondrous sight,
My soul was captivated by its gleam;
As morning breaks, and chases darkest night,
So did thy beauty banish every dream.
For in thine eyes, a gentle fire did burn,
And on thy lips, a sweet and modest grace;
My restless heart no longer yearned to turn,
But found its haven in that lovely place.
No earthly art can capture such a hue,
No poet's words describe thy perfect mien;
Thou art a vision, beautiful and true,
A peerless mistress, and a matchless queen.
    So, when I gaze on thee, my senses reel,
    And all the depth of boundless love I feel.

###320###
The shifting seasons, in their constant round,
Bring forth their beauty, and their sad decay;
From winter's slumber, silent, cold, and bound,
To summer's warmth, that soon must pass away.
The budding spring, with promise in its air,
Gives place to summer, crowned with golden light;
Then autumn paints the trees beyond compare,
Before the coming of the icy night.
Yet 'midst this change, where all things yield to time,
My constant love doth steadfastly remain;
Unmoved by seasons, or by frost or rime,
It blooms eternal, 'midst joy and pain.
    For though the world may alter and decline,
    My faithful heart is ever truly thine.

###321###
When wasteful Time with ruin lays all low,
And beauty's frail estate doth swift decay,
Doth make the strongest fortresses to go,
And steal the glory of each passing day;
Then think, my love, what chance thy form shall have,
Against the tyrant's scythe, so sharp and keen,
If nought but dust thy tender flesh shall save,
When winter's breath hath chilled the summer green?
Yet in these lines, thy youth shall ever bloom,
When marble monuments to dust are turned,
Defying Time's inevitable doom,
By zealous verse, thy memory is burned.
So long as men can breathe, or eyes can see,
So long lives this, and this gives life to thee.

###322###
My mistress' eyes are nothing like the sun;
Coral is far more red than her lips' red;
If snow be white, why then her breasts are dun;
If hairs be wires, black wires grow on her head.
I have seen roses damask'd, red and white,
But no such roses see I in her cheeks;
And in some perfumes is there more delight
Than in the breath that from my mistress reeks.
I love to hear her speak, yet well I know
That music hath a far more pleasing sound;
I grant I never saw a goddess go;
My mistress, when she walks, treads on the ground.
And yet, by heaven, I think my love as rare
As any she belied with false compare.

###323###
Shall I compare thee to a summer's day?
Thou art more lovely and more temperate:
Rough winds do shake the darling buds of May,
And summer's lease hath all too short a date:
Sometime too hot the eye of heaven shines,
And often is his gold complexion dimm'd;
And every fair from fair sometime declines,
By chance, or nature's changing course, untrimm'd;
But thy eternal summer shall not fade,
Nor lose possession of that fair thou ow'st;
Nor shall Death brag thou wander'st in his shade,
When in eternal lines to time thou grow'st:
So long as men can breathe, or eyes can see,
So long lives this, and this gives life to thee.

###324###
When in disgrace with fortune and men's eyes,
I all alone beweep my outcast state,
And trouble deaf heaven with my bootless cries,
And look upon myself, and curse my fate,
Wishing me like to one more rich in hope,
Featured like him, like him with friends possess'd,
Desiring this man's art, and that man's scope,
With what I most enjoy contented least;
Yet in these thoughts myself almost despising,
Haply I think on thee,—and then my state,
Like to the lark at break of day arising
From sullen earth, sings hymns at heaven's gate;
For thy sweet love remember'd such wealth brings
That then I scorn to change my state with kings.

###325###
From fairest creatures we desire increase,
That thereby beauty's rose might never die,
But as the riper should by time decease,
His tender heir might bear his memory:
But thou, contracted to thine own bright eyes,
Feed'st thy light's flame with self-substantial fuel,
Making a famine where abundance lies,
Thyself thy foe, to thy sweet self too cruel.
Thou that art now the world's fresh ornament,
And only herald to the gaudy spring,
Within thine own bud buriest thy content,
And, tender churl, mak'st waste in niggarding.
Pity the world, or else this glutton be,
To eat the world's due, by the grave and thee.

###326###
O, never say that I was false of heart,
Though absence seem'd my flame to qualify.
As easy might I from myself depart
As from my soul, which in thy breast doth lie:
That is my home of love: if I have ranged,
Like him that travells I return again,
Just to the time, not with the time exchanged,
So that myself bring water to the main.
Then think my love, though absence did remove me,
Thy spirit still did with my spirit dwell;
And in these lines thou ever shalt approve me
True in my fix'd intent, when others fell.
For no such change shall ever stain my name,
If you be true, and I have felt no blame.

###327###
When I do count the clock that tells the time,
And see the brave day sunk in hideous night;
When I behold the violet past prime,
And sable curls all silver'd o'er with white;
When lofty trees I see barren of leaves,
Which erst from heat did canopy the herd,
And summer's green all girded up in sheaves
Borne on the bier with white and bristly beard,
Then of thy beauty do I question make,
That thou among the wastes of time must go,
Since sweets and beauties do themselves forsake
And die as fast as they see others grow;
And nothing 'gainst Time's scythe can make defence
Save breed, to brave him when he takes thee hence.

###328###
Thy glass will show thee how thy beauties wear,
Thy dial by thy watch will tell thy hour,
The vacant leaves of thy youth's book appear,
And tell how many graces thou dost pour
Into the lines where wrinkles now do dwell,
And furrow deep the brow that once was fair.
Thou art not what thou wert; the truth to tell,
Thy fading grace doth warn thee to beware
Of time's swift foot, which steals away thy prime,
And mocks the boast of youth with sudden age;
For every flower that blooms in summer's clime
Must yield to winter's cold and frosty rage.
Then let thy beauty in thy verse abide,
And so defy oblivion's swelling tide.

###329###
Not marble, nor the gilded monuments
Of princes, shall outlive this powerful rhyme;
But you shall shine more bright in these contents
Than unswept stone, besmear'd with sluttish time.
When wasteful war shall statues overturn,
And broils root out the work of masonry,
Nor Mars his sword nor war's quick fire shall burn
The living record of your memory.
'Gainst death and all-oblivious enmity
Shall you pace forth; your praise shall still find room
Even in the eyes of all posterity
That wear this world out to the ending doom.
So, till the judgment that yourself arise,
You live in this, and dwell in lovers' eyes.

###330###
Let me not to the marriage of true minds
Admit impediments. Love is not love
Which alters when it alteration finds,
Or bends with the remover to remove:
O no! it is an ever-fixed mark
That looks on tempests and is never shaken;
It is the star to every wandering bark,
Whose worth's unknown, although his height be taken.
Love's not Time's fool, though rosy lips and cheeks
Within his bending sickle's compass come;
Love alters not with his brief hours and weeks,
But bears it out even to the edge of doom.
If this be error and upon me proved,
I never writ, nor no man ever loved.

###331###
When I have seen by Time's fell hand defaced
The rich proud cost of outworn buried age;
When sometime lofty towers I see down-razed,
And brass eternal slave to mortal rage;
When I have seen the hungry ocean gain
Advantage on the kingdom of the shore,
And the firm soil win of the watery main,
Increasing store with loss, and loss with store;
When I have seen such interchange of state,
Or state itself confounded to decay;
Ruin hath taught me thus to ruminate,
That Time will come and take my love away.
This thought is as a death, which cannot choose
But weep to have that which it fears to lose.

###332###
Poor soul, the centre of my sinful earth,
Fooled by those rebel powers that thee array,
Why dost thou pine within and suffer dearth,
Painting thy outward walls so costly gay?
Why so large cost, having so short a lease,
Dost thou upon thy fading mansion spend?
Shall worms, inheritors of this excess,
Eat up thy charge? Is this thy body's end?
Then, soul, live thou upon thy servant's loss,
And let that pine to aggravate thy store;
Buy terms divine in selling hours of dross;
Within be fed, without be rich no more:
So shalt thou feed on Death, that feeds on men,
And Death once dead, there's no more dying then.

###333###
My love is as a fever, longing still
For that which longer nurseth the disease,
Feeding on that which doth preserve the ill,
Th' uncertain sickly appetite to please.
My reason, the physician to my love,
Angry that his prescriptions are not kept,
Hath left me, and I desperate now approve
Desire is ghastly, which my body wept.
Past cure I am, now reason is past care,
And frantic-mad with evermore unrest;
My thoughts and my discourse as madmen's are,
At random from the truth vainly express'd;
For I have sworn thee fair, and thought thee bright,
Who art as black as hell, as dark as night.

###334###
The expense of spirit in a waste of shame
Is lust in action; and till action, lust
Is perjured, murderous, bloody, full of blame,
Savage, extreme, rude, cruel, not to trust,
Enjoy'd no sooner but despised straight,
Past reason hunted; and no sooner had,
Past reason hated, as a swallow'd bait,
On purpose laid to make the taker mad:
Mad in pursuit, and in possession so;
Had, having, and in quest to have, extreme;
A bliss in proof, and proved, a very woe;
Before, a joy proposed; behind, a dream.
All this the world well knows; yet none knows well
To shun the heaven that leads men to this hell.

###335###
When in the chronicle of wasted time
I see descriptions of the fairest wights,
And beauty making beautiful old rhyme
In praise of ladies dead and lovely knights,
Then, in the blazon of sweet beauty's best,
Of hand, of foot, of lip, of eye, of brow,
I see their antique pen would have express'd
Even such a beauty as you master now.
So all their praises are but prophecies
Of this our time, all you prefiguring;
And, for they look'd but with divining eyes,
They had not skill enough your worth to sing:
For we, which now behold these present days,
Have eyes to wonder, but lack tongues to praise.

###336###
O from what power hast thou this powerful might,
With insufficiency my heart to sway?
To make me live upon thy frown or light,
And with a word my spirit to dismay?
I know not what, but when I look on thee,
A strange compulsion binds my captive will,
That though my soul desires to wander free,
It finds itself enthrall'd by thy sweet skill.
Thy voice, thy form, thy every gentle grace,
Doth hold me fast in bonds I can't undo,
And though I strive to flee this charming place,
My faithful heart will ever turn to you.
So in this thrall, content I will remain,
And count my service as my greatest gain.

###337###
To me, fair friend, you never can be old,
For as you were when first your eye I eyed,
Such seems your beauty still. Three winters cold
Have from the forests shook three summers' pride,
Three beauteous springs to yellow autumn turn'd
In process of the seasons have I seen,
Three April perfumes in three hot Junes burn'd,
Since first I saw you fresh, which yet are green.
Ah! yet doth beauty, like a dial-hand,
Steal from his figure, and no pace perceived;
So your sweet semblance, which I most command,
As erst my heart doth hold, is not bereaved
Of that fair youth whereon my spirit fed,
But in my verse, thy beauty is not dead.

###338###
Mine eye and heart are at a mortal war,
How to divide the conquest of thy sight;
Mine eye my heart thy picture would bar,
My heart mine eye the freedom of that right.
My heart doth plead that thou in him dost lie,
A closet never pierced with crystal eyes,
But with the owner's figuring thought doth fly
To cull his beauty's form, and thence arise
A fresh idea; whereas thine eye's proud gloss
Doth challenge that which it doth from thee bring,
And to the outward object's fine-spun floss
Doth all the honour and attraction fling.
With right hereof a question they do make;
But neither can the other's plea forsake.

###339###
When my love swears that she is made of truth,
I do believe her, though I know she lies,
That she might think me some untutor'd youth,
Unlearned in the world's false subtleties.
Thus vainly thinking that she thinks me young,
Although I know my days are past the best,
Simply I credit her false-speaking tongue:
On both sides thus is simple truth suppress'd.
But wherefore says she not she is unjust?
And wherefore say not I that I am old?
Oh, love's best habit is in seeming trust,
And age in love loves not to have years told:
Therefore I lie with her and she with me,
And in our faults by lies we flatter'd be.

###340###
No more be grieved at that which thou hast done:
Roses have thorns, and silver fountains mud;
Clouds and eclipses stain both moon and sun,
And loathsome canker lives in sweetest bud.
All men make faults, and even I in this,
Authorizing thy trespass with compare,
Myself corrupting, salving thy amiss,
Excusing thy sins more than thy sins are;
For to thy sensual fault I bring in sense,
Thy adverse party is thy advocate,
And 'gainst myself a lawful plea commence:
Such civil war is in my love and hate,
That I an accessary needs must be
To that sweet thief which sourly robs from me.

###341###
My love, when cruel Time thy beauty shall consume,
And furrow'd brow show where thy youth did lie,
When golden locks are turn'd to silver gloom,
And fading roses from thy cheek do fly,

Then shall the world, which now doth feast its sight
Upon thy grace, lament thy altered state,
And weep to see thee banish'd from the light,
By ravening years, and unrelenting fate.

But in these lines, thy perfect form shall live,
And painted praise shall mock death's fell decree,
A lasting breath thy poet's art shall give,
That unborn eyes may gaze upon of thee.

So shalt thou shine, when suns no longer burn,
And in my verse, eternal youth return.

###342###
When I behold the fleeting hours race,
Like hurried shadows o'er a summer's field,
And see how youth doth vanish from its place,
To age's frosty grip, at last to yield,

Then doth my mind unto reflection turn,
Upon the blooms that perish ere their prime,
And how the sun, though bright, must cease to burn,
Consumed by all-devouring, ruthless Time.

Each moment stolen from life's vibrant store,
Doth whisper cautions to the listening ear,
That beauty's transient grace shall be no more,
And all we cherish soon must disappear.

Save what in verse or memory we find,
A lasting solace for the troubled mind.

###343###
Let not my love be deem'd a changing thing,
That alters when it alteration finds,
Nor for light cause its steadfast faith unstring,
Like fickle wind that shifts with every winds.

For true affection, rooted deep and strong,
Doth scorn the tempests of uncertain days,
It bears the burdens, righteth every wrong,
And brighter glows through tribulation's haze.

Though beauty fade, and youthful vigour flee,
And fortune's wheel doth turn in endless round,
My heart, dear friend, shall ever rest with thee,
On ground where constancy is ever found.

So long as breath doth warm this mortal clay,
My love for thee shall never know decay.

###344###
From those bright orbs, where golden light doth dwell,
My soul draws solace in its deepest night,
A silent language that no tongue can tell,
A star to guide me with its gentle might.

For in their depths, a universe resides,
Of truths unspoken, mysteries profound,
Where virtue's pure and gentle spirit hides,
And peace eternal may at once be found.

Oft have I watch'd their sympathetic gleam,
When sorrow's shadow cross'd my troubled face,
Dispelling darkness, like a waking dream,
And filling all my being with sweet grace.

Let envious Time their lustre never steal,
For in their gaze, my very self I feel.

###345###
When dull invention seeks in vain to rise,
And sluggish thoughts refuse to take their flight,
My weary pen then doth no words devise,
But wanders lost within the paper's white.

Then do I call upon my dearest Muse,
Whose sacred fire can make the dullest gleam,
And from her fount, new inspiration choose,
To fashion verse as bright as any dream.

She doth impart a vigour to my hand,
And bids my spirit soar on joyful wing,
Unlocks the secrets of each fertile land,
And teaches every heartfelt note to sing.

Without her aid, my labours were in vain,
But with her touch, I live and write again.

###346###
Behold the spring, how brief her sweet domain,
When tender buds their emerald robes unfold,
And blossoms bright do grace the verdant plain,
Ere autumn's breath doth turn them pale and cold.

The cuckoo's call, the nightingale's soft lay,
A fleeting melody in summer's air,
Shall swiftly pass, and vanish with the day,
Leaving the boughs of winter bleak and bare.

So too, our joys, like flowers of the field,
Do bloom awhile, then wither and decay,
And all that beauty Nature's bounty yield,
Is but a moment's grace, then stol'n away.

But in remembrance, beauty may reside,
A treasure held, though all the seasons glide.

###347###
When heavy sighs escape the burdened breast,
And troubled thoughts like clouds obscure the sun,
When weary spirit finds no moment's rest,
And all life's pleasantries appear as none,

Then doth a gentle hand, a kindly word,
Bring solace to the heart that's sore distrest,
A quiet truth, by loving whispers stirr'd,
To banish shadows and restore the blest.

For in companionship, true healing lies,
A balm for wounds that time can scarce amend,
A mirror showing comfort in bright eyes,
A faithful spirit, loyal to the end.

So let us share our grief, our joys embrace,
And find in love a sweet, enduring space.

###348###
The mind, a treasury where thoughts are stored,
Doth keep account of joys and sorrows past,
Each precious moment tenderly deplored,
Or triumphs sweet, that were too good to last.

Through memory's lens, we see what once did bloom,
The faces dear, the scenes of youthful play,
It chases shadows from the present gloom,
And brings again the light of yesterday.

Though Time's cold hand may steal all else away,
And age's frost upon our temples spread,
This inner sun retains its constant ray,
A vital current for the living dead.

So let us cherish, ere the fading night,
The sweet remembrance, pure and ever bright.

###349###
When reckless youth, with headstrong, fiery zeal,
Doth rush headlong where caution fears to tread,
And wounds itself, unmindful how to heal,
By empty hopes and foolish passions led,

Then doth experience, stern but kindly guide,
Unfold the lessons by past errors taught,
And bids the soul lay youthful scorn aside,
To seek the treasures wisely to be sought.

For Time, the master, though he steal our grace,
Doth also bring a clearer, wiser sight,
And paints new lines upon a thoughtful face,
Reflecting truth, dispelling folly's night.

So let us learn, and cast our faults away,
And greet with knowledge each succeeding day.

###350###
Seek not in gilded show or painted face,
The lasting essence of affection's bond,
For outward glitter holds a fleeting grace,
And beauty's flower soon doth lie beyond.

But rather search for truth within the soul,
Where virtue dwells, and honest thoughts reside,
A spirit pure, that makes the wounded whole,
And from deception's mask doth ever hide.

For love that's founded on a base so true,
No storm can shake, no envy can undo,
It doth endure when all things else seem new,
And shines a constant star, forever through.

So judge not by the eye, which oft deceives,
But by the heart, which truly apprehends.

###351###
When thou art far, and shadows fill my room,
And silent hours slowly drift along,
My heart doth languish in a cheerless gloom,
And finds no comfort in the merriest song.

The birds outside, though sweetly they do call,
Their joyous notes seem hollow to my ear,
For absence builds a high and lonely wall,
And magnifies each silent, gathering tear.

No sun doth warm, no moon doth shed her light,
With half the lustre when thou art away,
And day itself seems cloaked in endless night,
A sombre hue upon the brightest day.

Return, my love, and banish all my pain,
And bid my lonely spirit smile again.

###352###
Behold the morn, in russet mantle clad,
Doth chase the shadows from the sleeping earth,
And with its light, makes every creature glad,
Awak'ning joy and giving solace birth.

The eastern gate, where golden Phoebus dwells,
Unbars its portals to his fiery car,
And o'er the hills, a radiant glory swells,
Dispelling darkness, near and very far.

The dew-kiss'd grass doth sparkle on the ground,
As nature wakes to greet the new-born day,
And gentle breezes breathe a whispered sound,
To bid the lingering mists to steal away.

So let us rise, with spirits light and free,
And welcome morning's sweet tranquility.

###353###
When weary flesh its daily toil hath done,
And anxious thoughts do vex the troubled brain,
Then gentle Sleep, by Nature's hand begun,
Doth draw her curtain o'er life's bitter pain.

She binds the senses in a silken thread,
And lays the mind in peaceful slumber deep,
Consigns to rest the living and the dead,
And secrets from the waking world doth keep.

A sweet oblivion, from all cares set free,
A brief release from sorrow's heavy chain,
That bids the soul in placid dreams to flee,
And grants new strength to face the day again.

So let us yield unto her soft command,
And wake refresh'd, by her restoring hand.

###354###
The year doth turn, and seasons swiftly glide,
From verdant spring to summer's golden heat,
Then autumn's bounty, where rich fruits abide,
Till winter's chill makes nature's heart retreat.

Each brings its beauty, transient and unique,
The budding leaf, the blossom's fragrant breath,
The harvest store, the snow-clad, frozen peak,
A cycle marking life, and hinting death.

So doth our life, through various stages run,
From childhood's morn to youth's tempestuous noon,
Till mellow age completes what was begun,
Beneath the pale and silent, watching moon.

Let us embrace each change, as fate doth send,
And learn contentment till life's journey end.

###355###
I ponder oft what makes my spirit quail,
When silence falls where once sweet words did flow,
And wonder if thy constancy might fail,
Or if my heart doth nurse a groundless woe.

The shadow of a doubt, a whispered fear,
Doth creep unbidden to my troubled mind,
And questions rise, though none I wish to hear,
Lest bitter truths I sorrowfully find.

Perhaps the fault lies not in thee, my dear,
But in myself, who doubt too readily,
And conjures ghosts that never do appear,
To mar the peace I might enjoy with thee.

Oh, banish then these spectres from my breast,
And let my love in trusting comfort rest.

###356###
When storms of fortune on my vessel beat,
And cruel winds conspire to break my mast,
When lonely thoughts within my bosom meet,
And hope itself seems fleeting, fading fast,

Then doth thy presence, like a steady shore,
Bring solace to my soul, and calm my fear,
A faithful haven I can turn unto,
Whose steadfast comfort ever draweth near.

No flatterer's breath, nor feigned, deceitful smile,
Doth mark thy truth, which shines sincerely bright,
But honest counsel, free from selfish wile,
A beacon strong, through sorrow's darkest night.

So bless'd am I, to count thee as my friend,
Whose loyal spirit waits until the end.

###357###
The world doth prize the glitter and the show,
The outward garb, the rich and costly stone,
And rarely seeks the hidden worth below,
Where virtue's quiet essence may be known.

For oft a heart that beats with modest grace,
Enshrines more honour than a king's array,
And purer beauty in a humble face,
Than all the jewels wealth can e'er display.

Let shallow minds pursue the empty praise,
And fawn on greatness, howsoe'er it rise,
But give me truth, in unadorned ways,
That shines with light, reflected from the skies.

For true nobility, in spirit dwells,
Beyond the pomp that worldly grandeur sells.

###358###
When crumbling stone and ancient structures fall,
And monuments, by time consumed, decay,
When dust and rust devour the princely hall,
And mighty empires slowly fade away,

Yet shall the poet's consecrated rhyme,
Outlive the breath of kings, the warrior's strife,
Defy the ravages of ruthless Time,
And grant to truth an everlasting life.

For words, when skill'd, a deathless form do take,
More potent far than bronze or marble hard,
And for the ages, lasting echoes make,
By beauty's hand, and genius safeguard.

So let the world its fleeting glories prize,
My verse shall soar, beyond all change and lies.

###359###
No summer's day can boast thy grace entire,
Nor gentle breeze can match thy spirit free,
Nor blooming rose possess such sweet desire,
As doth within thy lovely being be.

The fleeting cloud, that drifts across the blue,
Though bright its edges, soon will fade from sight,
And transient gleams, like morning's tender hue,
Are lost when day asserts its fuller light.

So fragile beauty, born of earthly dust,
Doth quickly wane, and know its fading hour,
And all that seems so fair, so sweet, so just,
Succumbs at last to Time's consuming power.

But truth of heart, and virtue's firm control,
Shall ever shine within a constant soul.

###360###
When last of breath from mortal coil doth part,
And silent dust doth claim what once was bright,
When cold oblivion stills the vibrant heart,
And draws a curtain on life's fading light,

Then shall the grave, with solemn, dark embrace,
Hold firm thy form, removed from earthly view,
And Time's relentless hand shall quite efface,
The living image, vibrant, fresh, and new.

But fear thou not, though flesh to earth descend,
And spirit take its flight to realms unknown,
For in these lines, thy memory shall transcend,
And through my verse, thy deathless worth be shown.

So shalt thou live, when marble tombs decay,
And conquer death, through this immortal lay.

###361###
When summer's lease is done and autumn nigh,
And youthful beauty doth begin to fade,
Then cruel time doth steal from every eye,
The rosy blush that nature once displayed.
For wrinkled age will conquer all too fast,
And steal the glory from thy golden hair,
The strength of youth, too quickly it is past,
Leaving but shadows of what once was fair.
Yet, in these lines, thy grace shall ever dwell,
A monument against time's ravening maw,
So long as men can breathe, or eyes can spell,
Thy beauty shall transcend all mortal law.
Thus, though thy form to dust must turn and cease,
My verse shall grant thy memory sweet release.

###362###
Mine eyes do crave the sight they cannot gain,
My heart doth ache for what it holds so dear,
And every moment brings but greater pain,
Since thou, my life, no longer dost appear.
Like one who seeks a star in deepest night,
And finds but clouds that mock his yearning gaze,
So do I wander, lost for want of light,
Through gloomy valleys and through sunless days.
Oh, absence, tyrant, thou dost sting and wound,
And make my spirits sink to lowest ebb,
No solace in this wretched world is found,
Caught in despair's intricate, endless web.
Return, sweet love, and banish sorrow's sting,
Or cease my breath, and end what suffering bring.

###363###
The fleeting breath of man, how soon it flies,
And mortal beauty yields to time's decay;
The proudest towers crumble 'neath the skies,
And all that lives must surely pass away.
Yet cunning art can hold the fleeting form,
And limn a face, though life itself be gone,
Defying death, outliving flood and storm,
And shining bright when centuries have flown.
So in my verse, thy grace I strive to keep,
That future ages may thy worth behold,
When earth's cold bosom holds thee in her sleep,
Thy story shall through living lines be told.
Thus, though thou fade, my rhymes shall make thee live,
More than all treasure earth can ever give.

###364###
Why should my heart so oft be vexed and sore,
When gentle skies do beam with golden light?
And why my spirit troubled to its core,
When nature paints the day with hues so bright?
'Tis not the world, nor fortunes cruel decree,
That plants these thorns within my troubled breast,
But inward thoughts, that ceaseless torture me,
Denying peace and banishing all rest.
Oh, wretched mind, that canst not find repose,
But feeds on shadows, born of doubt and fear,
Each joy it finds, a darker sorrow shows,
And drowns all comfort in a bitter tear.
Then let me sleep, and dream of happier things,
Until a truer dawn new promise brings.

###365###
When first I saw thy face, a radiant gleam,
My soul, enthralled, did mark thee for its own,
As poets gaze upon a waking dream,
And find therein a beauty never known.
Thy eyes, like stars, did cast a gentle fire,
That warmed my blood and set my heart ablaze,
Inspiring thoughts that lift my spirit higher,
And chase away the gloom of former days.
No painted mask, no artifice of skill,
Could e'er approach the grace that dwells in thee;
Thou art thyself, beyond a painter's will,
A living wonder for all men to see.
Then let thy light forever guide my way,
And turn my darkest night to brightest day.

###366###
Comparing thee to roses, fresh and fair,
Whose tender petals ope to greet the sun,
I find a beauty none can quite compare,
When summer's fleeting pageant is begun.
But roses fade, their brief perfection done,
And scattered leaves confess their swift decay,
When winter's icy conquest hath been won,
Their fragrant glory stolen far away.
Yet thy dear charm, no season can impair,
No blighting frost can dim thy vibrant hue;
My love for thee doth banish all despair,
And keeps thy verdant spirit ever new.
So long as breath in mortal men shall bide,
Thy changeless beauty shall with verse reside.

###367###
Behold the lily, how it springs in pride,
And mocks the common weeds that stand below;
Its snowy beauty cannot long abide,
For every blossom to the earth must go.
So too, dear youth, thy comely grace shall fade,
And time, a thief, thy golden locks will steal;
A wrinkled brow, by weary seasons made,
Thy once bright promise shall at last conceal.
Then use thy prime, ere age thy strength doth numb,
And plant thy self in issue, fair and good,
That from thy beauty, fairer seed may come,
To live anew, in vital flesh and blood.
Else, when thy glass is run, and thou art gone,
Thy peerless form shall never more be known.

###368###
My love is like the tide, that ebbs and flows,
Now full of ardour, now with cold despair;
A fickle wind that as it listeth, blows,
And leaves my heart to wrestle with its care.
One moment, blest by thy approving smile,
I feel my spirit soar to heights above;
The next, thy frown, with treachery and guile,
Doth cast me down from all my hopeful love.
Oh, constant heart, where can such refuge be?
From shifting sands of change and false delight?
To find a truth, unwavering and free,
To anchor thoughts through day and darkest night.
But since thou art so changeful, so untrue,
My heart must learn to live apart from you.

###369###
When we are parted, how the hours drag slow,
Each minute seems a day, each day a year;
My spirits droop, my joys refuse to grow,
And every sound doth whisper doubts and fear.
The sun itself seems shorn of all its might,
And flowers lose the glory of their bloom;
The stars do pale, and lose their wonted light,
As if the world were clad in endless gloom.
So much of beauty hides when thou art gone,
So much of music dies within my ear;
I walk alone, until the weary dawn,
Recalls the time when thou wert ever near.
Then haste, sweet love, and banish sorrow's night,
And fill my empty world with joy and light.

###370###
If nature's gifts, which time doth quickly waste,
Were not renewed, but perished with each hour,
Then beauty's lineage would be quite erased,
And lovely forms would lose their vital power.
But wisely she doth teach us to impart
Our fairest substance to a younger race,
To engrave our essence on a willing heart,
And leave behind a legacy of grace.
Then heed her call, let not thy beauty die,
But make some fair copy, ere thy life be done,
That future ages, when they gaze thereby,
May see thy charms beneath a youthful sun.
So shalt thou live, though dust thy body claim,
Preserved forever in another's name.

###371###
The gaudy spring, with blossoms freshly strewn,
Doth yield its sweetness to the summer's hold;
And summer's pomp, beneath the harvest moon,
Gives way to autumn's russet, brown, and gold.
Then winter comes, with icy breath and chill,
And strips the trees of every verdant leaf,
A silent promise of a spring to fill
The barren branches, bringing sweet relief.
So too our lives, in seasons do unfold,
From tender youth to age's hoary brow;
A story written, centuries old,
With fleeting joys, and sorrows we allow.
But love, like spring, shall ever bloom anew,
If faithful hearts remain both firm and true.

###372###
My love is just, though others may deride,
My faith unshaken, though the storms may blow;
No envious tongue can turn my heart aside,
No cruel rumour make my feelings low.
For I have known thy spirit, pure and bright,
And seen the truth that shines within thine eyes,
A constant star, through sorrow's darkest night,
A haven safe from all that life denies.
Let fools condemn, and slanderers invent,
Their shallow words can never reach my soul;
My steadfast heart on thee is wholly bent,
And shall remain, though ages onward roll.
For in thy love, my truest self I find,
Leaving the shifting world and doubts behind.

###373###
When in disgrace with fortune and men's eyes,
I all alone beweep my outcast state,
And trouble deaf heaven with my bootless cries,
And look upon myself, and curse my fate,
Wishing me like to one more rich in hope,
Featured like him, like him with friends possessed,
Desiring this man's art, and that man's scope,
With what I most enjoy contented least;
Yet in these thoughts myself almost despising,
Haply I think on thee, and then my state,
Like to the lark at break of day arising
From sullen earth, sings hymns at heaven's gate;
For thy sweet love remembered such wealth brings,
That then I scorn to change my state with kings.

###374###
That time of year thou mayst in me behold
When yellow leaves, or none, or few, do hang
Upon those boughs which shake against the cold,
Bare ruined choirs, where late the sweet birds sang.
In me thou seest the twilight of such day
As after sunset fadeth in the west,
Which by and by black night doth take away,
Death's second self, that seals up all in rest.
In me thou see'st the glowing of such fire
That on the ashes of his youth doth lie,
As the deathbed whereon it must expire,
Consumed with that which it was nourished by.
This thou perceivest, which makes thy love more strong,
To love that well which thou must leave ere long.

###375###
The sun doth rise with glory in the east,
And mount the heavens with a fiery stare,
To warm the world, from greatest unto least,
And banish shadows from the earthly air.
But ere he doth his daily course conclude,
He sinks again into the western wave,
Leaving the world in pensive solitude,
Consigned to darkness, like an open grave.
So human life, a transient, brief display,
From morn of birth to evening's swift decline,
A fleeting moment, gone ere one can say,
A passing beauty, not forever thine.
Then let us seize the joy that present brings,
For future hours fly on silent wings.

###376###
Thou art more lovely and more temperate,
Than summer's blustering winds that shake the bud;
Thy gentle nature doth all storms abate,
And calms the tempest in my troubled blood.
Sometimes too hot the eye of heaven shines,
And often is his gold complexion dimmed;
And every fair from fair sometime declines,
By chance or nature's changing course untrimmed.
But thy eternal summer shall not fade,
Nor lose possession of that fair thou ow'st;
Nor shall death brag thou wander'st in his shade,
When in eternal lines to time thou grow'st.
So long as men can breathe or eyes can see,
So long lives this, and this gives life to thee.

###377###
What tongue can speak the wonders of thy grace?
What mortal pen can capture such a light?
My halting words cannot thy worth embrace,
Nor paint thy beauty, shining ever bright.
My humble Muse, though earnest in its plea,
Doth struggle hard to form a fitting praise,
For all its efforts fall far short of thee,
And falter 'midst thy soul's resplendent blaze.
Forgive, dear love, this poor and weak attempt,
To limn a form that Heaven's hand did mould;
From all false flattery I stand exempt,
My simple truth is more than finest gold.
Though words may fail, my heart shall ever try,
To show the love that cannot fade or die.

###378###
No truer love was ever sung or told,
Than that which binds my spirit close to thine;
A treasure richer far than gems or gold,
A sacred bond, by purest touch divine.
Though storms may rage, and cruel winds may blow,
And envious tongues may seek to sow discord,
Our steadfast hearts a constant flame shall show,
Protected by affection's mighty sword.
Let fleeting pleasures tempt the common mind,
And empty honours charm the shallow eye,
No false delights my faithful soul shall bind,
For in thy love, my lasting joys do lie.
So let us walk, united, hand in hand,
Through life's uncertain and perplexing land.

###379###
The world, a stage where weary actors play,
Their brief allotted parts, then quit the scene;
And life, a fleeting shadow of a day,
A moment's dream, that vanishes unseen.
Ambition's grasp, and avarice's plea,
The lust for power, and the thirst for fame,
Are but vain struggles for a phantasy,
A puff of breath, a momentary name.
But 'midst this folly, one true beacon shines,
A love unfeigned, that seeks no worldly prize;
A quiet haven, far from harsh designs,
Reflected in the kindness of thine eyes.
In such a love, my soul finds sweet repose,
A balm for all the bitter world bestows.

###380###
Let fickle fate her cruelest blows impart,
And scatter joys like leaves before the wind;
Let envious tongues conspire to break my heart,
And leave my spirit utterly maligned.
Yet shall my love for thee remain as firm
As rooted oak that scorns the winter's rage,
Unchanged by time, unyielding to the worm,
A deathless truth on life's bewildering page.
For thou art more than transient beauty's show,
More than the fleeting pleasures of an hour;
Within thy soul, such constant virtues grow,
That time itself shall not possess the power.
To dim my faith, or quench this sacred flame,
Which burns eternal, whispering thy name.

###381###
When lovely youth doth sport in summer's bloom,
And golden locks with gentle breezes play,
Doth then grim winter fill the heart with gloom,
And steal the fading glories of the day?
So swiftly doth each passing moment fly,
And beauty's transient grace doth make its stand,
Before time's ruthless scythe doth bid it die,
And pluck the fairest flower from the land.
Ah, would that art could stay its swift decree,
And paint the vibrant hues of youth anew,
Or hold a mirror to eternity,
To keep thy cherished image ever true.
But verse alone, a lasting monument,
Shall guard thy worth, though fleeting life be spent.

###382###
My love for thee doth mock the passing hour,
And scoffs at time, which all things else consumes,
It stands untouched by winter's icy power,
And laughs at summer's heat and autumn's fumes.
For what is beauty but a fleeting dream,
A momentary flash upon the stage,
If not upheld by love's eternal gleam,
Which binds the heart through every changing age?
Let fading roses shed their petals frail,
Let ancient stones succumb to slow decay,
My constant heart shall never know such fail,
But burn more brightly with each passing day.
So long as breath in mortal body dwells,
My truth for thee a timeless story tells.

###383###
Shall I compare thy grace to morning's light,
When dappled sunbeams pierce the misty air?
Or to the moon, that shines through darkest night,
And with a silver glow doth banish care?
No, for thy worth transcends these earthly shows,
Thy spirit gleams with an internal fire,
A gentle strength from which my comfort flows,
And lifts my soul beyond all base desire.
The lily fades, the rose doth droop and die,
The brightest stars may vanish from the sky,
But thy true virtue holds its sovereignty,
And grants to wretched life felicity.
Thus do I praise thee, though my words be weak,
For in thy face, pure heaven I do seek.

###384###
Unthrifty youth, why dost thou waste thy store,
When nature bids thee propagate thy kind?
Thy precious days, once gone, return no more,
And fading beauty leaves no trace behind.
Thou art a lease, granted by sovereign Time,
To bloom awhile, then yield to slow decline,
But if thou dost neglect thy vibrant prime,
No sweet renewal shall hereafter shine.
Consider well the garden's careful hand,
Which prunes the plant to make its fruit more grand,
So shouldst thou cherish life's entrusted seed,
To leave behind a fair and worthy breed.
Else, when thy glass is run, and breath is fled,
Thou leav'st no self, but sleep'st among the dead.

###385###
When fickle Fortune turns her wheel unkind,
And lays her heavy hand on mortal state,
Or grief and care do vex the troubled mind,
And joy's bright promise meets an early fate;
Then do I turn to lines of sacred art,
Where poets' souls their deathless thoughts unfold,
And find a solace for my weary heart,
