And all my hopes like summer blossoms fade,
I seek not comfort in decree of fate,
Nor in the promises that men have made.
For in thy beauty, doth my spirit find
A solace proof against all worldly harm,
A balm to heal the wounds of troubled mind,
A shelter sure from every coming storm.
Let kingdoms fall, and ancient cities rust,
Let empires crumble into dust and sand,
My loyal love for thee shall e'er be just,
While this poor verse holds steadfast in my hand.
For whilst men breathe, or eyes can read these lines,
So long lives this, and this gives life to thine.

###644###
The fleeting world doth teach us sorrow's sting,
As summer's green gives way to autumn's gold,
And joyful birds that erst did sweetly sing,
Are silenced by the winter's bitter cold.
The rose's blush, that graced the early morn,
By noon doth droop and scatter on the ground;
Thus every mortal thing to death is born,
And beauty's lease but for a while is found.
So too our days, swift as a shadow pass,
And all our glories hasten to their doom,
Reflected briefly in a fragile glass,
Before we vanish to the silent tomb.
Then let us love, whilst yet we have our breath,
Ere envious Time doth seal our eyes in death.

###645###
Lo, in thy face, the spring of youth I see,
A garden rich with blossoms fresh and fair;
Why dost thou hoard this beauty but for thee,
And waste thy prime, consumed by lonely care?
The world doth crave a fruit from such a tree,
That future ages may thy grace recall;
But if thou diest, and leavest no progeny,
Thy image then shall perish, root and all.
For nature's intent is to propagate,
To lend her gifts and see them multiplied,
Lest precious forms submit to cruel fate,
And virtue's seed forever be denied.
Then marry thee, and let thy beauty bloom,
Lest with thy passing, beauty finds its tomb.

###646###
Mine eye doth watch, what time thy form is far,
And grieves to know how distance doth divide;
As mariners who seek a guiding star,
So doth my soul for thy return abide.
No fleeting fancy holds my heart in thrall,
Nor sudden passion doth my senses bind;
But constant truth, that answers nature's call,
A love sincere, of truest, noblest kind.
Let changeful winds blow foul or fair above,
Let worldly trials vex my mortal state,
My steadfast faith, and everlasting love,
Shall hold thee dear, despite opposing fate.
For come what may, or fortune's harsh decree,
My truest self doth ever rest with thee.

###647###
When I behold the swift-consuming sand,
That steals the moments from our briefest day,
And see how beauties perish from the land,
Swept by the stream of Time's unceasing sway;
When ancient oaks, that stood for centuries,
Are felled by storms and crumble into dust,
And monuments, that once defied the breeze,
Yield to decay, and fall to rust and rust;
Then do I grieve, that nothing can endure,
But all things fade, however bright they seem,
And even love, whose promise stands so pure,
Must wake at last from life's delightful dream.
Yet in my verse, thy memory shall be,
A timeless flower, safe from time's decree.

###648###
My thoughts are not so fair as they should be,
Nor doth my tongue the proper praises frame;
When I would speak the worth I find in thee,
My humble words but put thy grace to shame.
For how can language, built of common clay,
Describe the light that doth from thee proceed?
As well might darkness strive to conquer day,
Or barren ground bring forth a fruitful seed.
I lack the skill, the eloquence, the art,
To paint thy virtues in their true array;
My mind's invention plays a feeble part,
And doth but tarnish what it would display.
Then pardon me, if silence be my plea,
For what I feel, no words can speak of thee.

###649###
Where are the hours of sweet and gentle youth,
That danced like fawns upon the morning dew?
And where the vows of everlasting truth,
That once my ardent spirit did imbue?
Alas, they're fled, like shadows on the plain,
Chased by the sun, or scattered by the breeze;
And in their place, a sorrow doth remain,
A quiet ache, that finds no heart-felt ease.
For time, with cruel and unrelenting hand,
Doth steal our vigour, and our beauty blight,
Leaving but memories in a barren land,
To mock the brilliance of a vanished light.
Then let me mourn what joy did once possess,
And find some solace in my heart's distress.

###650###
Thy presence shines, a beacon in the night,
To guide my vessel through life's stormy seas;
Thy gentle smile doth fill my soul with light,
And banish all my sorrows and unease.
No greater joy than to behold thy face,
No sweeter music than to hear thy voice;
Thy every motion, filled with charming grace,
Doth make my weary spirit to rejoice.
As thirsty flowers long for morning dew,
Or parched lands crave the solace of the rain,
So doth my soul continually pursue
The tender comfort that from thee I gain.
Thou art my sun, my stars, my very air,
Without thy grace, my world would be despair.

###651###
Mine eye, instructed by my yearning heart,
Doth gaze on thee with unremitting quest;
But what it sees, plays but a fleeting part,
And cannot give my troubled spirit rest.
For outward shows, though pleasing to the sight,
Are but the shadows of a deeper truth;
And beauty's bloom, however fresh and bright,
Is but the flower of transient, tender youth.
My soul seeks more than colour, form, and line,
It longs to know the essence of thy mind,
The inner grace, that makes thy being shine,
A treasure richer than the world can find.
So let my heart, not eye, thy worth proclaim,
And burn for thee with everlasting flame.

###652###
Let others sing of beauty's brief domain,
Of fleeting charms that vanish with the years;
My constant love shall evermore remain,
Untouched by doubt, unclouded by my fears.
For what is beauty but a fragile mask,
That time, with cruelest hand, doth soon unbind?
A transient pleasure, a demanding task,
To captivate the eye and fickle mind.
But truest love, built on a loyal base,
Doth scorn the passage of the seasons' turn;
It finds new lustre in a time-worn face,
And brighter glows where other passions burn.
So shall my faith, in purest form, endure,
Whilst fickle fortunes change, and life is sure.

###653###
My heart doth burn, as though by fire oppressed,
When others praise the beauty thou dost bear;
A bitter serpent writhing in my breast,
Doth mock the love I fondly hold so dear.
For jealousy, a green-eyed monster, blind,
Doth conjure doubts where no such shadows lie,
And whispers treachery unto my mind,
Though truth and innocence look from thine eye.
Oh, vexing torment, born of too much love,
That sees a rival in each passing gaze!
As though thy heart from me would swiftly rove,
Lost in the labyrinth of worldly maze.
Forgive, dear one, this weakness I confess,
Born of my fear to love thee any less.

###654###
When gentle sleep my weary eyelids seals,
And consciousness surrenders to the night,
My restless spirit then its journey wheels,
To seek thy image, shrouded from the light.
For though my body lies in slumber deep,
My dreaming soul doth wander far and wide,
And in my visions, thy sweet form I keep,
A cherished guest, forever by my side.
But ah, what joy can fleeting dreams bestow,
When dawn awakes me to a barren day?
The phantom touch, the whispers soft and low,
Like morning mists, do vanish swift away.
Then would I sleep, to dream of thee again,
And lose myself within that sweet domain.

###655###
The golden sun, that gilds the morning's brow,
Doth climb its zenith, then begins to fade;
As swiftly doth our fleeting pleasure bow,
And vanish swift, as though it were unmade.
The blossoms fair, that greet the infant spring,
With tender hues and fragrance soft and sweet,
Are soon consumed by summer's scorching sting,
And cast as dust beneath our careless feet.
So too the joys that light our mortal span,
A momentary gleam, a fragile fire;
They mock our hopes, and flee before our plan,
And leave us longing with a vain desire.
Then seize the day, and hold each moment fast,
For fleeting joys are never made to last.

###656###
Shall I compare thee to a summer's day?
Thou art more lovely and more temperate:
Rough winds do shake the darling buds of May,
And summer's lease hath all too short a date:
Sometime too hot the eye of heaven shines,
And often is his gold complexion dimm'd;
And every fair from fair sometime declines,
By chance, or nature's changing course, untrimm'd;
But thy eternal summer shall not fade,
Nor lose possession of that fair thou ow'st;
Nor shall Death brag thou wander'st in his shade,
When in eternal lines to time thou grow'st.
So long as men can breathe, or eyes can see,
So long lives this, and this gives life to thee.

###657###
My cruel mistress, with her icy heart,
Doth scorn the ardour that within me glows;
She plays a cold and an unfeeling part,
And on my tender pleadings mercy shows
No jot, no whisper, but a harsh disdain,
As though my love were but a tiresome plea;
She binds me fast with an unyielding chain,
Yet grants no freedom, nor doth set me free.
Like moth to flame, I'm drawn to her bright eye,
Though all I find is torment and deep pain;
I yearn for comfort, yet my hopes deny,
The gentle solace I would fain attain.
Oh, wretched plight, to love where love's denied,
And bear the pangs of pride and scorn allied.

###658###
Let others boast of titles and of fame,
Of glittering riches, or of lineage high;
I place my trust in truth's enduring name,
And in the love that beams from thy dear eye.
For outward show, though splendid to behold,
Is often false, and fades with passing years;
As stories rich, in ancient tales untold,
Prove empty comfort, yielding only tears.
But genuine affection, deep and true,
Doth scorn the trappings of a gilded age;
It finds its worth in what the heart can do,
And writes its glory on a nobler page.
So let them shine in borrowed, fleeting light,
Whilst our true love burns ever pure and bright.

###659###
The fear of absence gnaws upon my soul,
Lest cruel fate should part us, dear, too soon;
And Time, that steals away beyond control,
Should snatch thy beauty 'neath a waning moon.
For every moment that I spend with thee,
A subtle dread doth shadow all my joy;
That such perfection should so transient be,
And earthly blisses time will swift destroy.
My heart doth ache, to think of future years,
When thy bright form might vanish from my sight,
And leave me drowned in melancholy tears,
To grope through darkness, yearning for thy light.
Then hold me fast, and banish all my dread,
Lest living love should slumber with the dead.

###660###
When all the world doth fade, and life is done,
And earthly honours turn to dust and rust,
When memory's thread is broken, one by one,
And mortal frames return to common dust;
Then shall my verse, if it hath any might,
Preserve thy image from the silent tomb,
And hold thy beauty 'gainst oblivion's night,
To triumph o'er the shadows and the gloom.
For in these lines, thy spirit shall reside,
A deathless essence, pure and ever new,
Beyond the reach of fortune's ebbing tide,
A steadfast monument, forever true.
So read, and live, when I am passed away,
And know my love outlasts life's fleeting day.

###661###
When forty winters shall besiege thy brow,
And dig deep trenches in thy beauty's field,
Thy youth's proud livery, so admired now,
Will be but tatter'd weeds, no longer wield.
Then being asked where all thy beauty lies,
Where all the treasure of thy lusty days,
To say within thine own deep-sunken eyes,
Were an all-eating shame and thriftless praise.
How much more praise deserved thy beauty's use,
If thou couldst answer, "This fair child of mine
Shall sum my count, and make my old excuse,"
Proving his beauty by succession thine.
This were to be new made when thou art old,
And see thy blood warm when thou feel'st it cold.

###662###
The fleeting joys that grace our passing days,
Like blossoms frail, too swiftly fall and die,
And leave us longing for their sunlit rays,
Whilst shadows deep across our spirits lie.
How oft we chase a bliss that will not hold,
A fragile dream that vanishes at morn,
And find our brightest hopes turn sad and cold,
Leaving the weary heart forlorn and worn.
Yet memory, that sweet and constant friend,
Doth hoard the treasures of each happy hour,
And doth a balm of quiet comfort send,
Against grim sorrow's overwhelming power.
So let us cherish what our past hath given,
A glimpse of beauty, a small taste of heaven.

###663###
My dearest love, whose heart is cold as stone,
Why dost thou spurn the warmth I offer free?
My loyal faith for thee hath ever grown,
Yet finds no haven in thy cruelty.
I gaze upon thy face, so fair and bright,
And mark the beauty that all men commend,
But in thine eyes I find no tender light,
Nor any promise that my pain shall end.
So must I wander, laden with my care,
A pilgrim lost upon a barren plain,
And breathe my sighs into the empty air,
My constant suit return'd with cold disdain.
Ah, would that Cupid's dart might pierce thy breast,
And bring to thee the love I long possess'd!

###664###
When cruel Time doth waste each earthly thing,
And beauty's fading bloom doth pass away,
And lofty towers to dusty ruin bring,
Consuming all that lives beneath the day,
Then shall my verse, with more than mortal might,
Preserve thy grace from death's oblivious sleep,
And hold thy perfect image in its light,
Whilst envious ages round about us weep.
For neither rust nor moth shall spoil this line,
Nor hungry flames consume its deathless store,
But through all woes thy memory shall shine,
As bright as when my hand did first explore
These hallowed words, which ever shall remain,
To speak thy praise, and conquer dark disdain.

###665###
Full many a promise did thy lips impart,
When first thy beauty held my soul enthralled,
And swore that constancy would fill thy heart,
Whilst other suitors vainly might have called.
But now, methinks, thy fond affection wanes,
As shifting clouds obscure the morning sun,
And in thy gaze a colder purpose reigns,
The gentle race of former love outrun.
Doth absence chill the fire of our vow?
Or hath some newer charm bewitched thine eye?
Alas, the tender warmth I treasured now
Seems but a jest beneath a faithless sky.
If true love perish thus, and friendships fade,
Then was my trust too carelessly assay'd.

###666###
When Fortune's wheel doth turn with cruel disdain,
And all my hopes are scatter'd to the wind,
I curse the hour that brought me forth to pain,
And leave sweet comfort far and far behind.
My spirit, vex'd, finds no repose or rest,
But tosses, storm-toss'd, on life's bitter sea,
And every good, by envious stars suppress'd,
Doth mock the wretched state allotted me.
Then I recall thy face, and all my woe
Is straight forgot, as dawn dispels the night,
And like the lark that hails the sun's first glow,
My heavy heart takes wing and seeks the light.
For thy dear love doth richer solace bring,
Than all the world could e'er afford a king.

###667###
O, what a torment doth possession breed,
When doubt and fear infest the lover's breast!
A serpent's venom, planted like a seed,
That steals away all comfort, peace, and rest.
To look on beauty with a jaundiced eye,
And see a rival in each passing gaze,
To mark each smile, each word, each gentle sigh,
And turn them to a thousand cruel assays.
This green-eyed monster, with its bitter sting,
Doth warp the soul and make the spirit blind,
And doth such cruel imaginings bring,
That truth itself can no sure succour find.
Oh, banish, love, this dire and hateful guest,
Lest it consume thy heart and lay it waste!

###668###
Like shadows vain that fleet across the day,
Or transient blossoms of the early spring,
So fragile life doth quickly pass away,
And to its final slumber soon doth bring.
The babe that laughs upon its mother's knee,
The ardent youth with hopes so fresh and bold,
The man mature, the aged, frail, to see
All yield to dust, and turn to silent mould.
Where are the kings that ruled with mighty hand?
Where are the beauties that did charm the sight?
All gone, like footprints on a shifting sand,
Lost to oblivion's dark and endless night.
But in the soul, a spark immortal lies,
That mounts triumphant to the deathless skies.

###669###
Where art thou, love, that dost my comfort keep?
My weary soul doth pine for thy return.
The restless hours, like bitter waters, creep,
And all my thoughts for thine own presence burn.
The sun doth rise, but brings no joy to me,
The stars look down upon a tear-stained bed,
And every morn doth but remind my plea,
That thou art absent, and my spirit dead.
Come back, my solace, and relieve my pain,
Let not thy servant languish thus forlorn,
And bid my heart to beat with joy again,
And welcome hope, anew with thee reborn.
For life without thy light is but a tomb,
A world of sorrow, fill'd with endless gloom.

###670###
Behold the spring, how fresh its colours bloom,
The budding trees put forth their tender green,
Dispelling winter's long and hoary gloom,
A joyful sight, a most refreshing scene.
The birds do sing their matins to the morn,
The gentle breezes whisper through the glade,
As if no human care had e'er been born,
Nor any bitter sorrow ever made.
Yet man, with all his subtle, plotting mind,
Doth fret and toil, and chase a fleeting prize,
Whilst nature's peace he often leaves behind,
And beauty passes by his heedless eyes.
Oh, that we might but learn her calm employ,
And find in simple things a truer joy!

###671###
When fickle fortune turns her smiling face,
And summer friends like swallows take their flight,
And in adversity, no warmth we trace,
But find ourselves abandon'd to the night,
Then shines the jewel of a faithful heart,
A steadfast soul, a comfort ever near,
That plays a true and uncorrupted part,
And banishes all doubt and every fear.
Such is the love, dear friend, that binds us twain,
More precious far than gold or kingly crown,
A gentle balm that soothes all worldly pain,
And lifts the spirit when it would fall down.
Long may this bond of sacred friendship last,
A beacon bright, when worldly joys are past.

###672###
How heavy fall the hours when thou art gone!
My heart, a prisoner, yearns for thy return,
And every moment, tedious and long,
Doth with a silent, secret sorrow burn.
The sun, though bright, appears with lesser ray,
The birds' sweet chorus lacks its wonted sound,
And all the world, which seem'd so fair by day,
Is but a barren waste on hallow'd ground.
Oh, hasten, love, and bring thy light anew,
Dispelling shadows that about me cling,
And paint the dreary world with joyful hue,
And bid my weary spirit rise and sing.
Come back, my spring, and chase away my night,
And fill my darkest days with gladsome light.

###673###
To gaze too long upon thy mirrored face,
And find in self alone thy chiefest prize,
Is to neglect the beauty of thy race,
And close thy heart unto a lover's sighs.
To outward show, though it be fair to gaze,
A transient mask that Time doth soon impair,
What profit yields such self-admiring ways,
When inward worth hath fled beyond compare?
O, learn betimes to cast thy self aside,
And let true merit be thy guiding star,
For empty pride doth ever swiftly glide
To dark oblivion, however far.
Seek lasting grace that doth thy soul adorn,
Lest thou awaken desolate and lorn.

###674###
The year doth turn, and seasons swift depart,
From verdant spring to summer's golden reign,
Then autumn's bounty, stealing every heart,
Before grim winter comes with icy chain.
So human life doth pass in swift array,
From tender childhood to youth's eager stride,
Then manhood's strength, that cannot long hold sway,
Till age and weakness hasten to our side.
Each stage doth bring its pleasure and its plight,
A fleeting joy, a sorrow soon forgot,
And all that once was bathed in morning light,
Returns to dust, as if it ne'er had got
A breath of life. So short our span below,
A brief illusion, and a passing show.

###675###
Though mountains rise and oceans wide divide,
And cruelest fate conspires to hold us far,
No earthly bounds can true affection hide,
Nor quench the light of love's eternal star.
For when the heart with genuine passion burns,
It leaps across all gulfs of space and time,
And to its dearest object ever turns,
With constancy that knows no waning clime.
So let the world with all its burdens press,
Let adverse winds tempestuously blow,
My steadfast spirit shall no less possess
The fervent love that in my soul doth grow.
For love, when pure, defies all mortal might,
And finds its triumph in eternal light.

###676###
Where once the rose did flaunt her velvet grace,
And blushing petals spoke of summer's prime,
Now wither'd leaves obscure that charming face,
And yield their beauty to encroaching time.
So too the cheek, where youth did paint its hue,
And in the eye a sparkling lustre shone,
Now bears the mark of seasons passing through,
Its former glory utterly o'erthrown.
Ah, cruel Time, that steal'st all things away,
And leav'st no trace of what was once so fair,
Thy hungry scythe doth make all life thy prey,
And strew its faded honours on the air.
Yet in my verse, thy beauty shall remain,
Safe from oblivion's grasp, and winter's bane.

###677###
If fault or blemish in thy form I find,
Or mark some shadow that doth dim thy light,
My truer judgement doth refuse to mind,
But holds thy image ever pure and bright.
For love, when deeply rooted in the soul,
Doth mend all flaws and make the imperfect whole,
And doth such grace and charm about thee roll,
That even nature's errors it makes droll.
So let the critics with their envious tongue,
Decry thy seeming faults, both small and great,
My loyal heart, which hath for thee long clung,
Shall praise thy worth, and elevate thy state.
For in mine eyes, no other can compare,
Thou art my heaven, beyond all earthly care.

###678###
The clock doth tick, and tells the passing hour,
Each moment lost, can ne'er return again,
And youth's brief bloom, that holds such gentle power,
Doth fade and fall, like blossoms in the rain.
My glass runs fast, my sands do quickly flow,
And wrinkles deep begin to line my face,
A solemn warning that I soon must go,
And yield my breath to Time's unyielding pace.
So let me ponder, ere my life be spent,
On deeds well done, and words of honest truth,
And what true love to others I have lent,
Ere chilly age doth steal my vital youth.
For when I lie within the silent tomb,
My spirit then shall triumph over gloom.

###679###
One fleeting glance from thy most tender eye,
Hath power to banish all my heavy care,
And makes the darkest clouds of sorrow fly,
Leaving my spirit light, beyond compare.
For in that gaze, a magic doth reside,
That calms the tempest of my troubled breast,
And doth my faltering heart securely guide,
To peaceful havens of eternal rest.
What need I then of fortune's fickle smile?
What need of honours, or of worldly praise?
Thy single look can all my woes beguile,
And light my pathway through life's darkest days.
So cast on me, sweet love, thy radiant sight,
And turn my winter's cold to summer's light.

###680###
When noble virtue, once so brightly pure,
Is stain'd by vice, and tarnished by ill deed,
The wounded spirit finds no lasting cure,
And seeds of sorrow in the bosom breed.
To see a mind, where wisdom held its sway,
Now warped by folly, or by passion led,
To watch the dawn of promise fade away,
And honour's banner by dishonour shred.
Alas, that beauty should consort with shame!
That honesty should wear a cheating face!
And that a soul, which bore a worthy name,
Should fall from grace, and lose its rightful place.
Such sights do grieve the heart, and cloud the eye,
To mark such ruin, and to sigh and cry.

###681###
When I consider everything that grows
Holds in perfection but a little moment,
That this huge stage doth all her pageants shows
And then by time receives her full comment;
When I perceive that men as plants do spring,
And in their prime youth gather strength and height,
Then wither as the seasons change and bring
The hoary winter, banishing all light;
Then of the general wreck I think on thee,
And that thy beauty must in time decay,
Unless my verse preserve thy memory,
Against oblivion's force to make its way.
So shalt thou live, though time doth thee consume,
My ink shall keep thy beauty from the tomb.

###682###
Shall I compare thee to a summer's day?
Thou art more lovely and more temperate:
Rough winds do shake the darling buds of May,
And summer's lease hath all too short a date:
Sometime too hot the eye of heaven shines,
And often is his gold complexion dimmed;
And every fair from fair sometime declines,
By chance, or nature's changing course untrimmed;
But thy eternal summer shall not fade,
Nor lose possession of that fair thou ow'st;
Nor shall Death brag thou wander'st in his shade,
When in eternal lines to time thou grow'st:
So long as men can breathe or eyes can see,
So long lives this, and this gives life to thee.

###683###
Mine eye hath played the painter and hath stelled
Thy beauty's form in table of my heart;
My body is the frame wherein 'tis held,
And perspective it is best painter's art.
For through the painter's art is largely shown
The shape of things, yet nothing can transcend
The living grace that in thy face is known,
Which doth my soul's own portraiture commend.
To find this cunning art, my thoughts employ,
To trace each lineament of thy sweet face,
That thus within my breast thou shouldst enjoy
A dwelling fair, a most beloved place.
Yet for all this, to me thou art not near,
For my heart's room thy image doth not clear.

###684###
When I do count the clock that tells the time,
And see the brave day sunk in hideous night;
When I behold the violet past prime,
And sable curls all silvered o'er with white;
When lofty trees I see barren of leaves,
Which erst from heat did canopy the herd,
And summer's green all girded up in sheaves,
Borne on the bier with white and bristly beard;
Then of thy beauty do I question make,
That thou among the wastes of time must go,
Since sweets and beauties do themselves forsake
And die as fast as they see others grow:
And nothing 'gainst Time's scythe can make defence,
Save breed, to brave him when he takes thee hence.

###685###
If my dear love were but the child of state,
It might for Fortune's fire be tried in vain;
Or if it stood for sport to fickle fate,
Then might my soul indeed lament and plain.
But since my heart's firm truth is well assured,
And no tempest can shake my rooted mind,
By constant faith from all false shows secured,
I joy to think my love cannot be blind.
Let others seek their pleasure in things new,
And constant objects with new forms compare;
My love to thee shall ever be found true,
Though change and ruin bring their sad repair.
My constancy no varying thoughts shall stain,
But with my love, my life shall still remain.

###686###
How like a winter hath my absence been
From thee, the pleasure of the fleeting year!
What freezing thoughts did in my bosom lean,
When I from thee no welcome news could hear!
As in the season of the frozen days,
The birds are mute, and earth in darkness lies,
So in my heart, no cheering song displays
Its hopeful note, when thou art from mine eyes.
But when thy longed-for presence doth appear,
Like to the spring, thy beauty doth unfold,
And chase away the sorrow and the fear,
That held my captive spirit in its hold.
Then, like the sun, thy smiles my soul embrace,
And joy returns to fill its vacant space.

###687###
When in disgrace with fortune and men's eyes,
I all alone beweep my outcast state,
And trouble deaf heaven with my bootless cries,
And look upon myself and curse my fate,
Wishing me like to one more rich in hope,
Featured like him, like him with friends possessed,
Desiring this man's art and that man's scope,
With what I most enjoy contented least;
Yet in these thoughts myself almost despising,
Haply I think on thee, and then my state,
Like to the lark at break of day arising
From sullen earth, sings hymns at heaven's gate;
For thy sweet love remembered such wealth brings,
That then I scorn to change my state with kings.

###688###
Full many a glorious morning have I seen
Flatter the mountain tops with sovereign eye,
Kissing with golden face the meadows green,
Gilding pale streams with heavenly alchemy;
Anon permit the basest clouds to ride
With ugly rack on his celestial face,
And from the forlorn world his visage hide,
Stealing unseen to west with this disgrace.
Even so my sun one early morn did shine
With all triumphant splendor in my brow;
But out, alack, he was but one hour mine,
The region cloud hath masked him from me now.
Yet him for this my love no whit disdaineth;
Suns of the world may stain when heaven's sun staineth.

###689###
My love is as a fever, longing still
For that which longer nurseth the disease,
Feeding on that which doth preserve the ill,
The uncertain sickly appetite to please.
My reason, the physician to my love,
Angry that his prescriptions are not kept,
Hath left me, and I desperate now approve
Desire is health's decay, and life's untimely wept.
Past cure I am, now reason is past care,
And frantic-mad with evermore unrest;
My thoughts and my discourse as madmen's are,
At random from the truth vainly expressed;
For nothing this wide world I do despise,
But for what it denies my craving eyes.

###690###
Let those who are in favour with their stars
Of public honour and proud titles boast,
Whilst I, whom fortune of such triumph bars,
Unlooked for joy in that I honour most.
Great princes' favourites their fair leaves spread
But as the marigold at the sun's eye,
And in themselves their pride lies buried,
For at a frown they in their glory die.
The painful warrior famousèd for fight,
After a thousand victories once foiled,
Is from the book of honour razèd quite,
And all the rest forgot for which he toiled:
Then happy I, that love and am beloved,
Where I may not remove nor be removed.

###691###
No longer mourn for me when I am dead
Than you shall hear the surly sullen bell
Give warning to the world that I am fled
From this vile world, with vilest worms to dwell:
Nay, if you read this line, remember not
The hand that writ it; for I love you so,
That I in your sweet thoughts would be forgot,
If thinking on me then should make you woe.
O, if, I say, you look upon this verse
When I perhaps compounded am with clay,
Do not so much as my poor name rehearse,
But let your love even with my life decay,
Lest the wise world should look into your moan
And mock you with me after I am gone.

###692###
When forty winters shall besiege thy brow,
And dig deep trenches in thy beauty's field,
Thy youth's proud livery, so gazed on now,
Will be a tattered weed, of small worth held:
Then being asked where all thy beauty lies,
Where all the treasure of thy lusty days,
To say within thine own deep-sunken eyes,
Were an all-eating shame and thriftless praise.
How much more praise deserved thy beauty's use,
If thou couldst answer "This fair child of mine
Shall sum my count and make my old excuse,"
Proving his beauty by succession thine!
This were to be new made when thou art old,
And see thy blood warm when thou feel'st it cold.

###693###
Unthrifty loveliness, why dost thou spend
Upon thy self thy beauty's legacy?
Nature's bequest gives nothing, but doth lend,
And being frank she lends to those are free.
Then, beauteous niggard, why dost thou abuse
The bounteous largess given thee to give?
Profitless usurer, why dost thou use
So great a sum of sums, yet canst not live?
For having traffic with thyself alone,
Thou of thyself thy sweet self dost deceive.
Then how, when Nature calls thee to be gone,
What acceptable audit canst thou leave?
Thy unused beauty must be tombed with thee,
Which, used, lives th' executor to be.

###694###
Poor soul, the centre of my sinful earth,
Fooled by those rebel powers that thee array,
Why dost thou pine within and suffer dearth,
Painting thy outward walls so costly gay?
Why so large cost, having so short a lease,
Dost thou upon thy fading mansion spend?
Shall worms, inheritors of this excess,
Eat up thy charge? Is this thy body's end?
Then, soul, live thou upon thy servant's loss,
And let that pine to aggravate thy store;
Buy terms divine in selling hours of dross;
Within be fed, without be rich no more:
So shalt thou feed on Death, that feeds on men,
And Death once dead, there's no more dying then.

###695###
Tired with all these, for restful death I cry,
As to behold desert a beggar born,
And needy nothing trimmed in jollity,
And purest faith unhappily forsworn,
And gilded honour shamefully misplaced,
And maiden virtue rudely strumpeted,
And right perfection wrongfully disgraced,
And strength by limping sway disabled,
And art made tongue-tied by authority,
And folly doctor-like controlling skill,
And simple truth miscalled simplicity,
And captive good attending captain ill:
Tired with all these, from these I would be gone,
Save that, to die, I leave my love alone.

###696###
When I have seen by Time's fell hand defaced
The rich proud cost of outworn buried age;
When sometime lofty towers I see down-razed,
And brass eternal slave to mortal rage;
When I have seen the hungry ocean gain
Advantage on the kingdom of the shore,
And the firm soil win of the watery main,
Increasing store with loss, and loss with store;
When I have seen such interchange of state,
Or state itself confounded to decay,
Ruin hath taught me thus to ruminate,
That Time will come and take my love away.
This thought is as a death, which cannot choose
But weep to have that which it fears to lose.

###697###
Let me not to the marriage of true minds
Admit impediments. Love is not love
Which alters when it alteration finds,
Or bends with the remover to remove:
O no! it is an ever-fixèd mark
That looks on tempests and is never shaken;
It is the star to every wandering bark,
Whose worth's unknown, although his height be taken.
Love's not Time's fool, though rosy lips and cheeks
Within his bending sickle's compass come;
Love alters not with his brief hours and weeks,
But bears it out even to the edge of doom.
If this be error and upon me proved,
I never writ, nor no man ever loved.

###698###
My mistress' eyes are nothing like the sun;
Coral is far more red than her lips' red;
If snow be white, why then her breasts are dun;
If hairs be wires, black wires grow on her head.
I have seen roses damasked, red and white,
But no such roses see I in her cheeks;
And in some perfumes is there more delight
Than in the breath that from my mistress reeks.
I love to hear her speak, yet well I know
That music hath a far more pleasing sound;
I grant I never saw a goddess go;
My mistress, when she walks, treads on the ground:
And yet, by heaven, I think my love as rare
As any she belied with false compare.

###699###
When to the sessions of sweet silent thought
I summon up remembrance of things past,
I sigh the lack of many a thing I sought,
And with old woes new wail my dear time's waste:
Then can I drown an eye, unused to flow,
For precious friends hid in death's dateless night,
And weep afresh love's long since cancelled woe,
And moan the expense of many a vanished sight:
Then can I grieve at grievances foregone,
And heavily from woe to woe tell o'er
The sad account of fore-bemoanèd moan,
Which I new pay as if not paid before.
But if the while I think on thee, dear friend,
All losses are restored and sorrows end.

###700###
O, lest the world should task you to recite
What merit in my verse you see so great,
That all things else seem worthless in your sight,
And in your love should silently debate
The truth of honour, and the trust of love,
How many of my worthless leaves you read,
Which waste in time, and will no favour move,
While other poets in your thoughts are bred:
Then say the first, that I for you am made,
And that my love for you is still entire;
The second thus, that for your sake I played
The fool for love, and burned in self-same fire.
So shall you blame, and so shall I be free,
And you remain beloved, and love me.

###701###
When cruel Time doth steal our youth away,
And furrowed lines do mark the fairest brow,
And beauty's rose, once vibrant, must decay,
Then what solace may our spirits allow?
For swift-winged hours do haste to their cold end,
And fleeting joys like shadows quickly flee,
No lasting grace doth nature freely lend,
But all things bend to mutability.
Yet if my verse thy worth can truly bear,
And limn thy form in everlasting ink,
Then shalt thou live beyond all earthly care,
And 'gainst oblivion's tide shall never sink.
So in these lines, thy memory shall thrive,
When stones are dust, and men no longer live.

###702###
My love for thee, a steadfast, burning flame,
Doth light my path through life's perplexing maze,
No common passion can this ardour tame,
Nor dull the wonder of thy gracious ways.
As sunbeams chase the darkness from the sky,
Thy presence banishes all shades of fear,
And with a glance, thou mak'st my spirit high,
Dispelling sorrow when thou drawest near.
Oh, let not absence cool this sacred fire,
Nor let the world's harsh clamour make it cease,
For in thy heart is all my soul's desire,
And in thy gaze, my troubled mind finds peace.
So till my breath departs this mortal frame,
My soul shall echo with thy blessed name.

###703###
What mortal hand can paint thy matchless grace,
Or words contain the beauty of thy mind?
No earthly canvas could thy form embrace,
Nor poet's quill thy gentle soul define.
For in thine eyes, a heaven's light doth shine,
Reflecting virtues pure beyond compare,
A spirit noble, utterly divine,
That makes the common world appear more fair.
Though envious time may strive to mar thy face,
And steal the bloom from youth's delightful prime,
My steadfast verse shall hold thy youthful space,
And bear thy truth beyond the reach of time.
So live thou ever in this humble rhyme,
Defying age, and change, and all their grime.

###704###
When I behold the fading of the year,
And see the leaves in russet garments lie,
And hear the mournful winds lamenting near,
That whisper tales of beauty soon to die;
Then do I ponder on thy transient state,
How swift thy youth, like summer, takes its flight,
And dread the cruel decrees of envious fate,
That plunges all things lovely into night.
But yet my love finds comfort in this thought,
That though all earthly glories fade and fall,
The truest heart by time is never caught,
But answers still to beauty's urgent call.
So whilst thou liv'st, thy beauty I'll commend,
And love thee truly till my life shall end.

###705###
Shall I compare thee to a summer's day?
Thou art more lovely and more temperate:
Rough winds do shake the darling buds of May,
And summer's lease hath all too short a date:
Sometime too hot the eye of heaven shines,
And often is his gold complexion dimm'd;
And every fair from fair sometime declines,
By chance or nature's changing course untrimm'd;
But thy eternal summer shall not fade,
Nor lose possession of that fair thou ow'st;
Nor shall Death brag thou wander'st in his shade,
When in eternal lines to time thou grow'st:
So long as men can breathe or eyes can see,
So long lives this, and this gives life to thee.

###706###
My wandering thoughts, like ships upon the main,
Do seek a haven in thy tranquil breast,
And from the world's loud tumult and its pain,
They long to find a sweet and peaceful rest.
For in thy smile, a golden promise dwells,
A sacred balm for every grieving heart,
And by thy voice, my anxious spirit swells
With joy that naught but thy dear love impart.
But if thy favour from my sight should stray,
And fickle fortune turn thy face from me,
Then would my soul be lost in dark dismay,
And all the world a barren wilderness be.
So keep me ever in thy gentle mind,
That true delight I may forever find.

###707###
The weary sun, when he doth leave the sky,
Paints heavens red with his departing gleam,
A fading grandeur as the day doth die,
And slips away, as in a waking dream.
So beauty's self, though crowned with youth's bright ray,
Must yield at last to Time's unsparing hand,
And see its glory vanish and decay,
Like blossoms falling on a barren land.
Yet love, which springs from truth and spirit's core,
Doth mock the fleeting moments as they pass,
And finds new strength to cherish and adore,
Beyond the frail reflections in a glass.
Then let us love, and scorn what age can do,
Our hearts united, ever strong and true.

###708###
When in the chronicle of wasted time
I see descriptions of the fairest wights,
And beauty making beautiful old rhyme
In praise of ladies dead and lovely knights,
Then, in the blazon of sweet beauty's best,
Of hand, of foot, of lip, of eye, of brow,
I see their antique pen would have exprest
Even such a beauty as doth live in thee now.
So all their praises are but prophecies
Of this our time, all you prefiguring;
And, for they look'd but with divining eyes,
They had not skill enough your worth to sing.
For we, which now behold these present days,
Have eyes to wonder, but lack tongues to praise.

###709###
As nature's self doth change with every hour,
From budding spring to winter's icy hold,
And all things yield to an unyielding power,
Their fleeting stories in her book unrolled;
So doth my mood oft shift with varying winds,
Now high with hope, now steeped in deep despair,
As fortune's wheel my restless spirit finds,
And casts it down, or lifts it to the air.
But constant still, amidst this changing tide,
Thy sovereign image in my soul doth lie,
A fixed star, my true and faithful guide,
That brightens e'en when gloomy tempests fly.
So let the world its stormy troubles bring,
Thy love alone my steadfast heart shall sing.

###710###
The fleeting breath of fame, how soon it dies,
Lost in the echoes of a distant past,
And worldly honours melt before our eyes,
Like snows that vanish when the sun doth cast
His warming gaze upon the frozen plain.
No mortal triumph can defy the grave,
Nor earthly grandeur long its state sustain,
From Time's voracious maw, what hand can save?
But in the silence of a cherished thought,
Where deepest feelings find their secret place,
A lasting joy and truth is truly wrought,
Beyond the reach of ruin and disgrace.
So let my love, though simple, find its way,
And shine unquenched beyond life's briefest day.

###711###
When with the pangs of absence I am grieved,
And long for sight of thy beloved face,
My heavy heart feels utterly bereav'd,
And empty seems the world in every space.
Then fancy paints thy form before my mind,
In hues more vivid than the day can show,
And in that vision, solace I do find,
A fleeting joy, though real sorrows grow.
But oh, how cruel, this shadow of delight,
That mocks my yearning with a fond deceit,
And vanishes with morning's early light,
Leaving me longing, bitter, yet so sweet.
So come, my love, and banish every fear,
And make the real more present than the near.

###712###
My verse is poor, to sing thy boundless praise,
And clumsy words can scarce thy worth define,
How can I capture in these simple lays
A soul so gentle, utterly divine?
For when I strive to tell of thy bright eye,
Or limn the grace that in thy motion dwells,
My labour fails, and words like shadows fly,
And all my eager purpose quickly swells
With sense of lacking, for no tongue can frame
The perfect measure of thy spirit's truth,
Nor lend true lustre to thy cherished name,
Which shines more brightly than my fading youth.
Yet if these lines a spark of love can hold,
Thy beauty's story shall be ever told.

###713###
Some say that love is but a childish toy,
A fleeting passion of the tender years,
That with maturer wisdom we destroy,
And mock its promises, its hopes, its fears.
But they know not the depth of hearts entwined,
Nor feel the power of a faithful bond,
How truly soul to kindred soul can bind,
And reach beyond the bounds of life's demesne.
My love for thee, no ephemeral delight,
But firm as mountains, constant as the stars,
A guiding beacon through the darkest night,
That heals the spirit's deepest, hidden scars.
So let them scorn, who cannot understand,
This sacred union, by a heavenly hand.

###714###
The eye of heaven, though it shines so bright,
Doth oft perceive the shadows on the ground,
And sees the errors hidden from the light,
Where secret fault and folly may be found.
So too my love, though gazing on thy face,
Where beauty dwells in measure so sublime,
Doth mark the tiny flaws within thy grace,
The little trespasses of youth and time.
Yet this keen sight no whit doth make it less,
But rather strengthens what it holds so dear,
For true affection pardons with tenderness,
And sees thy virtues banish every tear.
So fear no scrutiny, my dearest friend,
My love shall cherish till the world doth end.

###715###
When nature's beauty fades before my sight,
And ancient glories turn to common dust,
And monuments surrender to the night,
And all things yield to time's corroding rust;
Then do I find in thee a fresh delight,
A blooming spring amidst the winter's chill,
A steady flame that burns through darkest night,
And holds its wondrous magic steadfast still.
For in thy spirit, truth and grace reside,
A beauty deeper than the outward show,
Which time's relentless current cannot hide,
But makes more radiant as the seasons flow.
So live thou ever, fairest and most dear,
And banish from my heart all doubt and fear.

###716###
How oft, when I am lost in thought profound,
And muse on fleeting joys and sorrows deep,
My restless spirit seeks a sacred ground
Where lasting peace its gentle watch may keep.
Then doth thy image rise before my eye,
A haven from the storm, a tranquil shore,
And all the anxious world doth seem to fly,
And troubles vex my burdened soul no more.
For in thy wisdom, solace I do find,
In thy true counsel, guidance for my way,
A precious treasure for the heart and mind,
That brightens every dark and gloomy day.
So be my star, my comfort, and my guide,
In whom my truest self may still confide.

###717###
No earthly gain, nor riches can compare
With the pure treasure of a heart so kind,
A gentle spirit, free from worldly care,
A love sincere, which few may hope to find.
For gold and jewels, though they sparkle bright,
Are but reflections of a passing show,
Their fleeting lustre cannot conquer night,
Nor lasting joy upon the soul bestow.
But true affection, by its own design,
Doth build a fortress 'gainst the blows of fate,
A bond unbreakable, a gift divine,
That enters hearts and triumphs o'er all hate.
So let me hold thy precious love so dear,
And banish every doubt and every fear.

###718###
The bitter pangs of absence wound me sore,
When thou art far, and I am left alone,
And crave thy presence, asking evermore
Where all my comfort and my joy have flown.
The sun itself seems dimm'd, and dull the day,
The birds sing sadly, and the flowers droop,
As if all nature mourns thy long delay,
And with my sorrow doth in sadness stoop.
Then do I count the minutes, slow and long,
And wish for wings to speed me to thy side,
To hear again thy sweet and gentle song,
And feel thy hand, my true and loving guide.
So haste thee home, my love, and banish grief,
And grant my yearning heart its sweet relief.

###719###
When in the glass I see my fading youth,
And time's harsh marks upon my brow appear,
I fear the swift approach of cruel truth,
That all things lovely vanish with the year.
My vibrant strength begins to ebb away,
My joyful spirit feels the heavy hand
Of age, that steals the promise of each day,
And makes me tremble at its stern command.
But then I look on thee, so fresh and bright,
And in thy youth, a solace I do find,
A mirror where my past holds gentle light,
And leaves the shadows of my age behind.
For in thy bloom, my spirit finds its stay,
And lives anew through thee, come what come may.

###720###
My tongue is tied, my words refuse to flow,
When I would speak of all I feel for thee,
A silent passion deep within doth grow,
Too vast for language, for the world to see.
For how can breath enclose such rich delight,
Or mortal phrases paint a truth so rare?
As stars unnumbered deck the velvet night,
So countless virtues in thy soul appear.
Thus, though my voice be mute, and faltering,
And weak my verse to tell thy worth divine,
My heart, in every beat, doth truly sing
The silent praises of a love like thine.
So let my silence speak what words suppress,
A boundless, tender, and true faithfulness.

###721###
When wasteful Time doth spoil the fairest things,
And makes the stoutest monuments decay,
How swift the course of earthly beauty springs,
To wither, lost and swiftly pass away.
What hand can stay his ever-conquering stride,
Or what defense against his might can stand?
When youth's bright morn must in his shadows hide,
And all delight be wrested from our hand.
Yet in this verse, where love doth make his bed,
Shall thy dear image deathless ever prove,
Though earthly bodies to the dust be led,
And conquer time by power of my true love.
So shalt thou live, beyond all fleeting breath,
And triumph o'er the tyrant, envious Death.

###722###
Thy gentle eye, the lamp that lights my way,
Doth cast a warmth upon my frozen heart,
And chase the shadows of my fears away,
Playing a sovereign and celestial part.
When sorrow's cloud obscures the morning light,
And bitter thoughts within my bosom dwell,
Thy beaming gaze doth make my spirit bright,
Dispelling all the gloom I know so well.
For in that glance, such potency resides,
As doth transform the common day to gold,
And where thy loving favor brightly guides,
My soul's deep secrets readily unfold.
So let thy grace shine on me evermore,
That I may love thee till my life is o'er.

###723###
The changing seasons tell a somber tale,
Of youthful spring that yields to summer's heat,
Then golden autumn, when the fruits prevail,
Before cold winter makes the world retreat.
So too our lives, from hopeful dawn to night,
Do run their course with swift and silent pace,
Each moment stealing from our precious light,
Leaving behind no permanent embrace.
But love, though born within this mortal frame,
Hath strength to scorn the passage of the years,
And burneth ever with a constant flame,
Beyond all earthly doubts and groundless fears.
For in its truth, eternity is found,
Where time's harsh rule can never quite confound.

###724###
My tongue is tied when I would sing thy praise,
For words, like shadows, mock my fond desire,
And cannot capture all thy lovely ways,
Nor fan enough my soul's devoted fire.
What greater art can paint thy visage true,
Or speak the virtues that within thee lie?
My feeble pen, though striving, proves untrue,
And fails to reach the heavens of thine eye.
The choicest phrases that I strive to find,
Seem but as dust before thy perfect grace,
Leaving my eager spirit far behind,
Unable to adorn thy hallowed place.
Yet know, dear heart, though silent be my plea,
My very soul doth wholly worship thee.

###725###
When nature's hand, with skill so rarely seen,
Hath wrought a form of such surpassing grace,
And decked thy visage with a noble mien,
To make thee fairest in earth's crowded space,
It doth beguile the eye to outward show,
And blind the mind to virtues deep within,
Lest men should fail thy inner worth to know,
And judge by beauty, where true life doth spin.
But wise discernment looks beyond the skin,
To find the spirit where true treasures gleam,
For outward lustre is but fragile thin,
A fleeting shadow of a waking dream.
So let thy soul, more bright than outward part,
Be known and loved by every honest heart.

###726###
How like a ghost my spirit wanders lost,
Since thou art gone, and darkness holds thy place,
Upon a sea where every wave is tossed,
And joy hath fled, leaving no certain trace.
The sun doth rise, yet brings no cheering ray,
The moon doth gleam, yet lights no lover's path,
Each passing hour doth only add dismay,
And mock my heart with sorrow's aftermath.
For every leaf that stirs upon the tree,
And every bird that sings its morning song,
But whispers echoes of thy loss to me,
Where silence now doth utterly belong.
Return, dear solace, quell this bitter strife,
And bring again the sunshine to my life.

###727###
Let those who list their loves on fortune's wheel,
And mark their vows by changeful moon and tide,
Believe that constant hearts can never feel
The steady force where true affections ride.
But mine own love, no fleeting summer's day,
Nor winter's chill, nor autumn's rich decline,
Can e'er persuade my loyal heart to stray,
Or quench the fervent spirit that is thine.
Though envious time may steal thy youthful bloom,
And lines of age upon thy forehead trace,
My steadfast faith shall conquer every gloom,
And find new beauty in thy altered face.
For truest love doth not decay with years,
But stronger grows, defying doubts and fears.

###728###
Behold the flower, how it blooms in pride,
Unfolding petals to the morning sun,
Then withers swift, its beauty cast aside,
When its brief race of splendor hath been run.
So doth fair youth, with momentary grace,
Pass like a shadow from our waking sight,
Leaving behind no permanent embrace,
But fading softly into endless night.
Then guard thy charm, ere envious years descend,
And steal the lustre from thy beaming eye,
Lest to the dust thy tender form doth tend,
And all thy loveliness should wholly die.
But let thy spirit live in poet's rhyme,
And brave the ravage of devouring Time.

###729###
When in the throes of unrequited pain,
My heavy heart doth yearn for thy sweet grace,
I look upon thy beauty, but in vain,
To find a mirror of my sorrow's trace.
Thy smiles are light, thy laughter soft and low,
Unburdened by the weight that presses me,
As if no single thought of my deep woe,
Could touch thy spirit, blithe and ever free.
Ah, cruel irony of fate's decree,
To bind my soul in such a hopeless thrall,
Whilst thou, oblivious, dost brightly flee,
Beyond the reach of my heart's desperate call.
Yet still I love, though love doth wound me sore,
And shall forever, till I am no more.

###730###
When sorrows mount, and heavy thoughts descend,
And all the world seems clad in sombre grey,
To thee, my truest solace, do I wend,
And banish troubles from my heart away.
For in thy presence, comfort I do find,
A gentle balm for every grievous smart,
And peace returns to my distracted mind,
As thou dost play a sweet and healing part.
The bitter winds of fate may fiercely blow,
And envious fortune try my soul to vex,
But thy steadfast spirit doth brightly glow,
Through all the trials that my being perplex.
So let me lean upon thy constant truth,
A haven safe from all of life's uncouth.

###731###
Dost thou believe my love, or deem it slight,
When oft I sigh and gaze with longing eye?
My heart, though hidden from thy outward sight,
Doth bear a witness that it cannot lie.
For every gesture, and each whispered word,
That from my lips for thy dear sake doth fall,
Is but an echo of a truth unheard,
A deeper passion that transcends them all.
If in thy breast some doubt perchance doth grow,
Or if my actions fail to make thee sure,
Then let my future hours plainly show,
How steadfastly my love will e'er endure.
For love like mine no fickle change can prove,
But burns eternal, by the stars above.

###732###
The raven locks that once adorned thy head,
Now streaked with silver, tell a passing year,
The rosy cheeks where youthful glow was spread,
Show lines of thought, a memory held dear.
And so the tree, that in the spring was green,
Doth shed its leaves when autumn's breath arrives,
To stand forlorn, a winter's barren scene,
As nature's ruthless cycle ever strives.
Yet in thy wisdom, beauty still doth dwell,
A deeper grace that time cannot efface,
A quiet majesty that casts a spell,
And lends a glory to thy aging face.
For soul's true worth doth ripen with the age,
And writes its beauty on life's final page.

###733###
How can we trust to Time's deceitful hand,
That steals our youth and bids our beauty fly,
Yet oft doth make the heart to understand,
And cherish visions from a bygone sky?
He takes the swiftness from the eager stride,
And dims the lustre of the sparkling eye,
But leaves behind a comfort deep inside,
A store of memories that cannot die.
For in the past, where all our joys reside,
He grants a haven from the present's sting,
And lets our spirits peacefully confide,
In whispered echoes that the moments bring.
So though he robs us with his cruel command,
He leaves us treasures, grasped in memory's hand.

###734###
My verse is poor, my spirit slow to rise,
When I attempt to sing thy matchless praise;
No lofty thoughts within my bosom lies,
To weave for thee a crown of golden lays.
I seek for words, but words do flee away,
Like frightened birds before the hunter's bow,
And leave me dumb, though much I long to say,
Of all the love that in my heart doth glow.
Perchance the Muses scorn my humble art,
Or I myself lack skill to strike the lyre,
To tell the beauty that adorns thy heart,
And fan the flame of my devoted fire.
Forgive my fault, if simple truth appears,
More eloquent than all the Muses' tears.

###735###
The blushing rose, whose beauty doth unfold,
In crimson raiment to the morning dew,
A fleeting wonder, fairer than fine gold,
Whose brief perfection nature doth imbue.
But ere the sun hath reached his zenith height,
Or evening shadows lengthen on the plain,
Her petals fall, despoiled of all their light,
And scattered lie, unheeded, by the rain.
So too, alas, doth mortal beauty fare,
A transient glory, lent for but a day,
To vanish swift, like breath upon the air,
And yield its bloom to time's devouring sway.
Yet in sweet verse, a magic to defy,
Thy perfect grace shall live, and never die.

###736###
When all is lost, and hope begins to wane,
And bitter thoughts like shadows fill the mind,
Then doth the power of enduring strain,
A solace for the weary spirit find.
Not in the pomp of kings, nor gilded halls,
Nor monuments of stone that touch the sky,
But in the breath of verse, which softly calls,
Doth true remembrance ever bravely lie.
For though the body turns to common dust,
And fading glories vanish from our view,
The poet's ink shall keep its sacred trust,
And give to life a meaning ever new.
So let my lines, however humbly writ,
Preserve thy truth, and conquer death with wit.

###737###
My dearest heart, why dost thou hold aloof,
And turn away thy gaze from my fond plea?
What cold disdain hath made thy spirit proof
Against the fervor that consumes in me?
If in my words some fault thou dost discern,
Or if my actions fail thy wish to meet,
Then speak the truth, that I may quickly learn,
And lay my errors humbly at thy feet.
For love like mine can brook no false pretense,
Nor bear the shadow of a dark surmise,
But craves the sunshine of thy frank defense,
Reflected brightly in thy honest eyes.
So grant me grace, thy favour to attain,
And ease my soul from this perpetual pain.

###738###
When day doth yield to night's embrace so deep,
And shadows lengthen, claiming all the light,
My thoughts unto thy absent presence creep,
And fill the darkness with thy form so bright.
The stars do gleam, like jewels in the sky,
But cannot match the lustre of thine eye,
The moon doth shine, yet seems to me to sigh,
For thy dear visage that is far thereby.
Then longed-for dawn doth pierce the fading gloom,
And with his golden arrows drives away,
The heavy thoughts that haunt my silent room,
And usher in the promise of new day.
Yet still I find, though day bring much relief,
Thy absence lends to every joy some grief.

###739###
When leaden sorrow weighs upon my breast,
And bitter sighing doth my spirit vex,
I seek in vain for comfort and for rest,
As weary thoughts my burdened mind perplex.
The very air doth seem to feel my pain,
The birds are silent, and the flowers droop,
As if the world would weep with me again,
And join my heart in its despairing scoop.
What potent spell hath cast this heavy pall,
Upon my soul, that joy can find no place?
And why must tears forever freely fall,
To mar the fairness of my youthful face?
Ah, let this grief pass swiftly from my sight,
And bring me back to reason's cheerful light.

###740###
When Fortune's frown doth cast its gloomy shade,
And worldly cares my weary spirit bind,
I turn to thoughts of thee, my gentle maid,
And leave all sorrows of the world behind.
For in thy grace, a sanctuary I find,
A peaceful haven from all bitter strife,
Where solace calms my agitated mind,
And lends new purpose to my fading life.
Let jealous tongues their venom freely pour,
And envious hearts their malice still deploy,
Their futile efforts I shall but ignore,
Content to revel in thy boundless joy.
For thy pure love, a treasure most divine,
Makes all the world's adversities benign.

###741###
When cruel Time doth steal fair beauty's bloom,
And wrinkle's furrows mark the youthful face,
Shall not our fleeting joys be sealed in tomb,
And all that's lovely yield to Time's swift pace?

The summer's warmth, by winter's frost subdued,
Doth shed its leaves, its verdant robes laid bare;
So too, dear friend, is nature's course imbued,
That all things bright must vanish into air.

But in these lines, thy grace shall ever shine,
When monumental brass shall cease to fade;
Thy living image, deathless and divine,
Shall keep thy memory from oblivion's shade.

So long as men can breathe, or eyes can see,
So long lives this, and this gives life to thee.

###742###
When envious Canker gnaws the tender Rose,
And beauty's fading hour doth swift appear,
And Summer's lease to Autumn's sorrow goes,
While chilling winds bring forth the dying year;

Then think not that my constant heart doth stray,
Or that my vows are writ on shifting sand;
Though seasons change and all things pass away,
My faith in thee shall ever firmly stand.

For true affection mocks at Time's cruel hand,
And doth defy his scythe and swift decay;
It builds its fortress on eternal land,
And shines more brightly at the close of day.

So whilst I breathe, and vital breath do draw,
My love for thee shall know no flaw.

###743###
When fleeting beauty hastes to make an end,
And youth's bright morn gives way to fading day,
Shall none but ruin on its steps attend,
And all its glory swiftly pass away?

Ah, if thou wouldst thy radiant self renew,
And from thy prime a fresh successor raise,
Thy perfect semblance might appear anew,
To charm the future with thy lovely gaze.

For by this means, though age thy form deface,
And time's fell sickle mow thy blossoms down,
A living mirror would reflect thy grace,
And wear thy image like a lasting crown.

So guard thy beauty from oblivion's thrall,
Lest nature's debt by thee should wholly fall.

###744###
When time hath ploughed his furrows in thy brow,
And silvered locks thy golden youth replace,
And all thy vibrant hues begin to bow
Before the winter of thy fading grace;

Then shall this humble verse, a faithful friend,
Preserve thy virtues from the greedy grave,
And to the future ages shall commend
The gentle spirit that these numbers save.

For monuments of stone do turn to dust,
And brass outworn by rain and wind decays;
But this my song, impervious to rust,
Shall echo forth through unremembered days.

So live thou ever in this poet's lay,
When envious death shall bear all else away.

###745###
When weary thoughts upon my spirit weigh,
And worldly cares besiege my troubled mind,
I turn to thee, my comfort and my stay,
A solace sweet, where gentle peace I find.

The storm and tempest of life's troubled sea
May rage without, and cruel fortune frown;
But in thy haven, safe and kept by thee,
My soul finds shelter, though the world sink down.

For in thy presence, all my sorrows flee,
And darkest shadows yield to thy bright ray;
Thy loving glance sets every captive free,
And drives the gathering glooms of grief away.

So be thou ever my secure retreat,
My life's dear balm, my refuge ever sweet.

###746###
The vernal buds proclaim the spring's return,
And tender shoots their leafy banners spread;
Yet brief the joys for which our spirits yearn,
Before their transient beauty lays them dead.

The violet, born with dewy morning's grace,
Unfolds its colours to the sun's warm gaze;
But soon it fades, and leaves no lasting trace,
A fleeting emblem of our passing days.

So earthly loves, like blossoms of a day,
May for a moment charm the wandering eye;
But ours, dear heart, shall never know decay,
A love that mocks at time, and will not die.

For in its depths, a truth profound doth dwell,
Beyond all change, a magic and a spell.

###747###
When I recall the joys that once were mine,
And youth's bright morning, now forever flown,
A heavy sadness on my soul doth twine,
For all that's cherished, vanished and unknown.

I sigh for friends long lost to death's cold sleep,
And weep afresh for love's departed grace;
My spirit grieves for promises to keep,
And shadows lengthen in life's vacant space.

Then, from these musings of a bygone age,
Thy image rises, beautiful and clear,
And turns the sorrow on my heart's dark page
To tender comfort, banishing all fear.

For in thy love, my losses are redeemed,
A truer joy than e'er I fondly dreamed.

###748###
Mark how the music, sweet and softly played,
Doth stir the soul with harmony profound,
And how each note, in tuneful consort made,
Unites in richness, through the air unbound.

When string doth answer string, and voice to voice
Doth lend its vibrant pulse, a joyous sound,
No single part alone can truly rejoice,
But all together, perfect strength are found.

So, when by discord vexed, thy spirit grieves,
And troubled thoughts within thy bosom start,
Let nature's concert bring thy soul reliefs,
And mend the fractures of thy wounded heart.

Learn then of music's sweet and binding sway,
To join in love, and cast all strife away.

###749###
Is't not a shame that thou, so richly blest
With Nature's gifts, and beauty's fairest dower,
Shouldst hoard thy treasures in thine own cold breast,
And let them perish in a single hour?

Thou hast a spirit bright, a mind acute,
A gentle grace that all the world admires;
Why dost thou yield to such a barren fruit,
And quench within thyself love's sacred fires?

The world cries out for offspring of thy kind,
To propagate the goodness thou dost hold;
But thou, unmindful, to thyself confined,
Dost let thy precious essence turn to mould.

Then ope thy heart, and let thy virtues spread,
Lest with thy dust, thy memory be dead.

###750###
Oh, wherefore dost thou turn away thy face,
And mask with cold disdain thy loving eye?
Hath my true heart committed some disgrace,
That thou shouldst treat my loyal suit so dry?

I do confess, my faults are not a few,
And errant youth hath led my steps astray;
But yet my soul, to thee alone stays true,
And longs for comfort at the close of day.

If e'er I wronged thee, let me then atone,
And cast thy anger from thy gentle breast;
My life's sole joy depends on thee alone,
In thy dear presence only can I rest.

Then grant me but one glance, one loving sign,
And make this weary, longing spirit thine.

###751###
Full many a man with outward show doth strive,
To win the world's applause and vain renown,
Whose painted smiles can seem but half alive,
Hiding the canker that consumes within.

He wears a cloak of virtue, fair to see,
And speaks with honeyed words and subtle grace,
But in his core, no true sincerity
Doth hold its sway, or find its rightful place.

But thou, dear friend, art fashioned otherwise,
No false disguise thy honest spirit cloaks;
Thy worth shines forth from truth-telling eyes,
Unburdened by hypocrisy's harsh yokes.

So let the world its hollow praises waste,
Thy truest value in my heart is placed.

###752###
When I behold the sun decline at night,
And fading glories paint the western sky,
I think upon the loss of youth's dear light,
And how all earthly things are born to die.

The strongest oak, that bravely bears the blast,
Must yield at last unto the axe's blow;
The summer's reign, how quickly is it past,
As winter's chilling winds begin to blow.

So man, however strong or fair of face,
Must one day fade and turn to common dust;
Leaving behind no vestige of his trace,
Unless preserved by love's eternal trust.

Yet fear not, love, though flesh to dust repair,
For in my verse, thy spirit shall be fair.

###753###
My friend, attend no more to flattering lures,
Nor let false pleasures lead thy heart astray;
For joy that quickly comes, as swift endures,
And leaves but sorrow at the close of day.

The painted smiles of fortune's fickle crew
May charm thine eye with superficial grace;
But deep within, no constancy is true,
Nor loyal kindness finds a dwelling place.

Choose rather paths where truth and honour guide,
Though rugged they may seem to fleshly sight;
For virtue's prize, though long it be denied,
Doth shine eternal with an inward light.

So steer thy course by reason's steadfast hand,
And build thy hopes on solid, lasting sand.

###754###
When I behold thy visage, passing fair,
And trace the lines where youth's sweet summer plays,
I marvel not at charms beyond compare,
That mock the transient glories of our days.

For outward beauty, though it hold the gaze,
Is but a mask that Time doth soon remove;
A fleeting flower that quickly fast decays,
Nor can it boast of everlasting love.

But 'tis thy spirit, gentle and sincere,
Thy constant temper, and thy thoughts so deep,
That bind my soul and banish every fear,
And vigils of affection bid me keep.

These are the gifts that truly will endure,
Thy truest essence, lasting, strong, and pure.

###755###
My heart, oft tossed on doubt's tempestuous wave,
Doth question if thy love will constant prove;
Lest fickle fortune, from a treacherous grave,
Should steal away the object of my love.

I know thy nature, open, frank, and kind,
And hold thy promises as sacred bond;
Yet whispers start to trouble my poor mind,
As shadows flit across life's fragile pond.

But when I look into thy candid eye,
And see the truth reflected shining there,
All vain suspicions from my bosom fly,
And sweet assurance banishes all care.

So banish doubt, my soul, and fear no more,
For loyal love doth anchor to the shore.

###756###
Let others sing of beauty's painted pride,
And seek for flatteries to deck their name;
My humble verse shall not such paths abide,
Nor fan with idle breath a borrowed flame.

I do not strive to make thy virtues seem
Beyond what nature's bounty hath bestowed;
Nor yet to catch thee in a flattering dream,
But show thy spirit as it truly glowed.

For truer worth needs no embellishing art,
It shines itself, beyond all outward show;
And in the quiet chambers of my heart,
Thy genuine graces ever brightly glow.

So take this offering, simple, pure, and plain,
More honest than a false and gilded gain.

###757###
As weary travellers long for evening's close,
And parched earth longs for soft and gentle rain,
So doth my spirit, seeking sweet repose,
Yearn for thy presence, to assuage its pain.

For thou art sun unto my darkest night,
And living spring unto my thirsty soul;
Without thy comfort, all my joys take flight,
And bitter waves of sorrow o'er me roll.

No power on earth can set my spirit free
From bonds of love that chain my heart to thine;
My very being is sustained by thee,
Thou art the essence of this life of mine.

So grant thy favour, lest I fall away,
And darkness claim me from the light of day.

###758###
The fairest flower must fade and lose its hue,
And summer's glory hath a fleeting stay;
The proudest towers, when ancient they wax through,
Must crumble down and yield to slow decay.

So too, the beauty that now holds thy gaze,
Shall in the mirror show a lessened light;
And all the praises of thy youthful days,
Be lost in shadows of approaching night.

But these my lines, carved with enduring art,
Shall keep thy semblance from oblivion's dust;
And bear thy image on through every heart,
A shining truth, a firm and lasting trust.

So read these words, when I am laid in ground,
And in their sound, thy beauty shall be found.

###759###
When stormy passions vex my troubled breast,
And reason's voice is drowned in wild despair,
My burdened spirit finds no place of rest,
But wanders forth, a victim to its care.

I strive to quell the tumult in my soul,
And bring some measure to my frantic grief;
But like a ship beyond all pilot's control,
My mind is driven, finding no relief.

O, that my thoughts could find a peaceful bay,
And anchor there from sorrow's ceaseless tide;
To banish shadows, and embrace the day,
And let serene contentment here abide.

Alas, these bitter storms within me rage,
And write my torment on life's cruel page.

###760###
The fading twilight warns of parting ways,
And stars begin to stud the vault of night;
Our pleasant converse, through these passing days,
Must yield to darkness, and withdraw from sight.

No more the joyful meeting of our eyes,
No more the laughter echoing in the air;
But silent memory, where comfort lies,
Shall guard thy image, beautiful and fair.

Though distance parts us, and though time may roll
His weary course, and bring forth many a change,
Thy cherished presence in my inmost soul
Shall find no bounds, nor suffer dull estrangement.

So fare thee well, my dear, my constant friend,
Until we meet again, beyond life's end.

###761###
When cruel Time shall waste thy tender bloom,
And furrow deep the brow that once was fair,
Shall beauty's light be lost in endless gloom?
Or leave some trace for memory to share?
The gilded pomp of youth must fade away,
And vigor's strength succumb to slow decay,
No mortal hand can hold back fleeting day,
Nor bid the swift-winged moments cease their sway.
Yet in these lines, thy grace I would impart,
A living portrait, proof against the smart
Of fleeting years that pierce the loving heart;
So shalt thou live, though outward form depart.
Thus deathless verse thy beauty shall rehearse,
And scorn the power of Time's consuming curse.

###762###
When fickle Fortune doth her favours move,
And transient clouds obscure the brightest day,
My constant heart shall still its true love prove,
Nor let harsh winds thy steadfast spirit sway.
Though earthly joys like shadows fleet from sight,
And worldly wealth should vanish with the night,
Thy virtues shine with an unfailing light,
More firm than mountains, conquer'd by no might.
Let seasons change, and spring to winter turn,
Let youth's bright colours fade to pallid hue,
My fervent flame shall never cease to burn,
But keep its vow, eternally fresh and true.
No change in thee can make my passion cease,
But deepen love and fortify my peace.

###763###
Those sparkling eyes, from whence my solace flows,
Do hold a heaven within their sapphire hue,
A gentle spirit their soft glance bestows,
And paints the world with colours fresh and new.
No painter's skill, though masterly and rare,
Can truly capture half their living grace,
Nor poet's verse, however sweet and fair,
Describe the beauty seated in thy face.
They are the mirrors of a soul so bright,
Reflecting wisdom, charity, and truth,
And banish shadows with their inner light,
A perfect emblem of enduring youth.
Ah, let them gaze and hold me ever fast,
For in their depths, my very soul is cast.

###764###
The transient glories that the world doth crave,
Of shining gold, and jewels bright and bold,
Are but as dust that winds about the grave,
A tale of vanity in moments told.
What boots it, then, to gather boundless store
Of fleeting treasures, purchas'd with much pain?
When Death's cold hand shall knock upon thy door,
All earthly riches shall prove utterly vain.
For what thou hast, thou canst not long retain,
And what thou seek'st, doth yield but brief delight;
No worldly gain shall ease thy spirit's pain,
When shadows gather and obscure thy light.
Then covet not what time doth soon corrupt,
Lest avarice thy spirit interrupt.

###765###
When marble structures crumble into dust,
And brazen towers yield to Time's sharp tooth,
When monuments to memory shall rust,
And beauty's fleeting flower lose its youth;
Then shall this verse, in humble guise array'd,
Outlive the wreck of palaces and kings,
And hold thy name, though kingdoms be betray'd,
As living proof of what true beauty brings.
For neither fire, nor war's destructive might,
Nor envious worms that feed on mortal clay,
Shall dim the splendour of thy spirit's light,
But thou shalt shine through each succeeding day.
So long as men can breathe, or eyes can see,
So long lives this, and this gives life to thee.

###766###
No summer's day can boast such tender grace,
Nor April's bloom so fair a form display;
For in thy mien, a sweeter joy I trace,
Than fleeting blossoms that but live a day.
The golden sun, though glorious and bright,
Doth often hide his face in clouds of gray,
And every beauty suffers from Time's blight,
Or chance's hand doth sweep it quite away.
But thy dear self with radiant virtue doth shine,
A truth eternal, fashioned all divine,
Whose worth no fading beauty shall decline,
But hold its lustre, ever truly mine.
So let my verse thy loveliness declare,
That future ages may thy worth compare.

###767###
When from thy presence I am forced to go,
My soul doth mourn and fills with bitter woe,
And all the world seems clad in garb of gloom,
As flowers fade that lack the sun's warm bloom.
My restless thoughts, like birds that seek their nest,
Do wander far, and find no place to light,
Until thy image, dear and ever blest,
Recalls their longing through the lonely night.
What comfort then can dull the bitter pain?
What cheer can soothe this anguish of the soul?
Until I see thy gentle face again,
No earthly balm can make my spirit whole.
Thus absence keen doth pierce my aching heart,
And makes me yearn for thee, when we must part.

###768###
When heavy burdens press upon my soul,
And clouds of sorrow dim life's hopeful gleam,
Thy gentle counsel makes my spirit whole,
A welcome solace, more than waking dream.
For in thy steadfast friendship I do find
A balm for wounds that worldly trials impart,
A loyal spirit, ever true and kind,
That binds my shattered pieces to thy heart.
Thou dost not chide my weakness, nor my fault,
But with a patience rare dost soothe my plea,
And raise my spirit from its low assault,
Teaching my troubled mind to lean on thee.
Oh, what a treasure, friend, thou art to me,
A haven safe, from worldly storms to flee.

###769###
How swiftly fly the moments of our years,
Like fleeting shadows on a sundial's face,
Each passing hour a new concern appears,
As time doth run its unremitting race.
The tender babe, whose smile delights the eye,
Doth soon assume the stature of a man,
And then, alas, his youthful vigour die,
Fulfilling nature's predetermined plan.
The ancient oak, that stood for centuries strong,
At last must yield to slow decay and rust,
And noble works, that once inspired song,
Shall turn to rubble, mingling with the dust.
So all things perish, and to nothing turn,
But love alone, a deathless flame shall burn.

###770###
When outward beauty, like a fading flower,
Doth yield its petals to the wintry blast,
And all the charms that graced youth's golden hour,
Are but dim memories of pleasures past;
Then shall my love, which doth no measure know,
Remain steadfast, unshaken, and unbent,
A hidden spring, whose ceaseless waters flow,
Though summer's verdant glory shall be spent.
For 'tis not form that doth my soul enthral,
Nor fleeting grace that holds my spirit bound,
But virtues deep, beyond the reach of all
That change or time on mortal things hath found.
So let all fade, save what my heart doth keep,
A love for thee, that never falls asleep.

###771###
When weary thoughts upon my spirit weigh,
And dull despair doth cloud my working mind,
I turn to thee, and chase the gloom away,
And in thy form, fresh inspiration find.
For what is art, but an endeavor'd strife
To capture beauty, transient and divine?
To breathe into cold lines the breath of life,
And make a fleeting shadow brightly shine?
My hand doth falter, and my spirit's sight
Oft grows obscure, by earthly cares oppress'd,
But thoughts of thee rekindle inner light,
